Statistics from the Ministry of Health: Our Nation's Excessive Mortality Rate 21

(Nanjing) According to statistics from the Ministry of Health, our nation's annual excess mortality rate (such as suicides, drownings, shootings, and all unjust deaths not due to illness) is approximately six million people. Based on an average age of ten years and an average annual consumption of fifty yuan, the annual loss due to excess mortality reaches 300 million yuan. The Ministry of Health also calculated the construction value, estimating that it could construct (1) 30,000 li of railways, (2) 800 factories, (3) 1,000 universities, (4) 100,000 elementary schools, (5) 5,000 hospitals, (6) 600 waterworks, and (7) 100,000 li of asphalt roads annually. Despite such an alarming loss, the people of our nation pay little attention. (Special Telegram, 19th)

Page 6

Far East Situation: U.S. Naval Policy Unchanged; Manila Naval Base Not Abandoned; Everything Depends on Japan 22

(London) Although British newspapers have recently predicted that the United States will close its naval base in Manila, according to statements obtained by Reuters today from several senior U.S. officials, the U.S. naval policy in the Far East will remain unchanged for the time being. It is reported that the United States has not made a decision to abandon the Manila naval base, nor is there any indication that it will withdraw the U.S. Asiatic Fleet stationed in the Philippines and abandon its naval bases throughout the Far East. The naval talks currently being held in London and the naval conference to be convened next year will affect the U.S. naval policy in the Far East, and this policy will depend on Japan's demands regarding naval ratios. The U.S. Asiatic Fleet can only be regarded as a police force, and is by no means capable of attacking others. The United States is indeed preparing to withdraw from the Philippine Islands, but the independence act stipulates the retention of the fleet stationed in the Philippines and supply stations, pending a decision by a conference to be convened two years after full independence. Full independence of the Philippines will be achieved in ten or twelve years. Therefore, the future of the Philippines as a naval base cannot be definitively decided until 1950. The United States has been developing Pearl Harbor in the Hawaiian Islands as its main base in the Pacific for many years, and has never planned to establish a strong naval base east of the Hawaiian Islands. According to the Washington Treaty, the United States agrees to maintain the status quo regarding naval bases in the Pacific, except for Hawaii. Therefore, Japan has obtained a guarantee that it will be protected from attack by the United States and Britain. Without a well-defended base, the United States or Britain can never wage an offensive war in the Far East with any hope of success. (Reuters Telegram, 19th)

Initial U.S.-Japan Naval Talks: Davis Meets with Matsudaira 23

(London) U.S. representative Davis and Japanese Ambassador to Britain Matsudaira discussed naval matters today. It is reported that Davis informed the Japanese Ambassador of the matters discussed yesterday with British Prime Minister MacDonald and others. Although the U.S. representative stated that any matter could be discussed, the difficult issue of naval ratios was not touched upon in yesterday's talks. Davis promised to inform Matsudaira of the various developments in the Anglo-American discussions. (Reuters Telegram, 19th)

Anglo-American Naval Negotiations: Real Work Begins Today 24

(London) The U.S. delegation went to the Prime Minister's residence on Downing Street today to exchange preliminary views on the scope of the 1935 naval conference. The real work will begin on Wednesday. Those who went to Downing Street this morning were Davis, the chief U.S. representative to the naval conference, Bingham, the U.S. Ambassador to London, Atherton, Counselor of the U.S. Embassy in London, and Admiral Leahy. The British officials who met them were Prime Minister MacDonald, Naval Minister Monsell, and Craigie, Head of the American Department of the Foreign Office. The meeting lasted about ninety minutes. It is reported that the U.S. delegation did not want to make suggestions, but only wanted to hear Britain's opinions and consider them. The first step will be relatively simple, merely selecting the date and location of the conference. The location is expected to be London. Once the date and location are decided, several technical issues may be considered, such as tonnage, vessels, and gun sizes. These are the main events, and the parties intend to exchange views in a timely manner to study them before the general conference. Political issues, such as ratios and the Pacific situation, are not to be discussed. The preliminary naval talks in London will all be bilateral in nature. After the Anglo-American discussions are completed, the British authorities will meet with the Italian delegation, and then with the Japanese delegation. Although France has not yet formally responded, it is expected that it will accept Britain's application. As each bilateral discussion proceeds, the information discussed will be communicated to all countries involved in the naval conference. It is now hoped that the results of the preliminary talks between the countries can clarify some points and make compromise easier to achieve, and to clear away all difficulties so that a successful agenda for the general conference can be drafted. (Reuters Telegram, 18th)

(London) The U.S. delegation held its first preparatory talks with the British authorities on Downing Street today for the 1935 naval conference, but the U.S. representatives were still unable to discern the position taken by the British government. The two sides have not yet exchanged views on general issues. However, the U.S. representatives will certainly oppose Japan's demands. What Japan is demanding is: (1) the implementation of total equality in naval tonnage; (2) each country should be able to allocate its due total tonnage according to its national needs. Therefore, the method of separately restricting the types of vessels according to the London Treaty will be abolished. Now that the talks between Britain and the United States have just begun, their direction will be greatly influenced by Japan's naval policy. According to the Japanese newspaper (Nichinichi Shimbun), Japan's intentions are roughly as follows: (1) demand that all countries reduce total tonnage and reduce the size of warships; (2) abolish the original 5:5:3 ratio of capital ships for Britain, the United States, and Japan, and adopt the principle of total tonnage limitation; (3) establish the principle of equality in armaments; (4) each country has the right to decide on its own national defense needs. The U.S. delegation cannot agree to the latter three demands, especially the second and fourth, because the U.S. representatives believe that doing so would be equivalent to absolute equality for the navies of all countries, and would give Japan the power to build any type of warship. Japan's naval sphere of activity is limited to the Pacific Ocean, while the United States must consider both the Pacific and Atlantic Oceans. The British Navy must be distributed among the seven oceans. Therefore, this theoretical equality is absolutely unequal in practice. The U.S. representatives will discuss this viewpoint with the British authorities. Therefore, the scope of the discussion will undoubtedly exceed procedural issues. The Japanese delegation will not arrive for another month, and the preliminary talks will be limited to strictly bilateral talks (i.e., Anglo-American, Anglo-Japanese, separate talks, rather than trilateral Anglo-American-Japanese talks). However, the Anglo-American parties will definitely consider the issues that the Japanese representatives will raise after their arrival. The British government's attitude has not yet been determined, and it is currently impossible to know. Today's meeting was merely routine in nature. The U.S. representatives are still taking a wait-and-see approach. Norman Davis will begin contacting Japanese Ambassador to Britain Matsudaira on Wednesday morning. (Havas Telegram, 18th)

Britain Has No Intention of Relinquishing Islands Adjacent to the United States 25

(London) British Prime Minister MacDonald stated firmly in the House of Commons today that Britain has never considered ceding Bermuda or other islands adjacent to the United States to the United States to settle war debts. A member of parliament said that these islands are of no value in British imperial defense. Another member asked if the Prime Minister intended to advise the United States to take over the Irish Free State. (Reuters Telegram, 18th)

Japanese Kwantung Army Conducts Major Air Defense Drill: Centered on Lushun-Dalian, Defending Against Russian Aircraft Attacks; Japanese Army to Hold Maneuvers in November; Red Army Gathers in Chita, Preparing for War 26

(Dalian) The air defense drill in Kwantung Province, centered on Lushun and Dalian, began at 7:00 AM this morning and is scheduled to end at 9:00 AM on the 21st. Lieutenant General Ando, Commander of the Lushun Fortress, serves as the Commander-in-Chief. The various army and navy units in Lushun-Dalian and members of the air defense corps are participating. Eighty aircraft from the Qiushui Zi Airport and Lushun's army and navy aircraft are being deployed. It is assumed that enemy aircraft are attacking Dalian and the Lushun naval port. Dalian is the central focus, so anti-aircraft guns, searchlights, and listening devices have been specially prepared. A blackout will be implemented at night. (Hualian Telegram, 19th)

(Tokyo) The joint air defense exercise of the Kwantung Province involving the army, navy, air force, and civilians began at 7:00 AM this morning, supervised by Jing Shan, Commander of the Lushun Fortress. Twenty military, naval, air force, and civilian aircraft and 5,000 members of the protection corps participated in the exercise. The aerial combat activity with five enemy aircraft was intense. The exercise will continue tomorrow and is scheduled to end at 7:00 AM on the 21st. (Den-tsu Telegram, 19th)

The army maneuvers for this year, scheduled for November, have been decided to be held in Gunma Prefecture. Lieutenant Colonel Mutaguchi, Chief of the General Affairs Section of the General Staff Headquarters, and Mr. Kane, an attendant, were dispatched to the area for investigation. Today, in Gunma Prefecture, they jointly announced the following with the General Staff Headquarters and the Imperial Household Ministry: (1) All participating units will complete assembly by November 10th; (2) The maneuvers will begin on November 11th; (3) A military review will be held on the 14th; (4) The units will be disbanded on the 15th; (5) A banquet will be held for qualified individuals on the 14th; (6) The headquarters has been designated to be in Gunma Prefecture; (7) The supervision department will be located at the Maebashi Normal School; (8) The military review will be held at the training ground of the 15th Infantry Regiment in Takasaki; (9) The Emperor is scheduled to visit various locations after the maneuvers. (Den-tsu Telegram, 19th)

(Harbin) According to Japanese sources, the Russian army believes that in the event of a Japanese-Russian war, the Japanese army will first use aircraft to destroy Chita in order to sever the connection between European Russia and Siberia. Therefore, General Blyukher, commander of the Far Eastern Red Army, has directed personnel in Chita to construct a large-scale airfield, which has recently been completed, with sixteen hangars and fifty fighter planes. Combat exercises are being conducted daily. There are also numerous anti-aircraft guns stationed in Chita, along with a large Red Army garrison. (Hualian Telegram, 19th)

Germany and Japan: Jointly Attacking Russia, Rumored to Have Reached a Secret Understanding 27

(London) A certain prominent figure recently returned from travels to both Soviet and German territories. An interviewer from the North-China Daily News visited him. According to him, the Russians now believe that there is a secret understanding between Germany and Japan to jointly attack Soviet Russia in the spring of 1935. By that time, the German withdrawal from the League of Nations will have become effective, and military preparations will also be complete. The official also claimed that Germany's goal is to seize the Baltic territories. The Germans are currently spending heavily on propaganda in that area and are also planning to occupy Ukraine, as that land is fertile and produces abundant resources, which would allow Germany to become self-sufficient. The German's second target is France, followed by Britain, because they attribute their defeat in the Great War entirely to Britain. However, Japan is no longer as confident of victory in the attack on Russia as it was before. The Russians are also very concerned about the recent meeting between the leaders of Italy and Germany, but they are very suspicious of the outcome of the meeting, believing that Hitler is merely a puppet. The official concluded by saying that Soviet Russia is now able to supply its own war materials and has even begun to produce nickel. (Special Dispatch from the North-China Daily News, 8th)

Amidst European Upheaval: France Actively Consolidates Alliances, Foreign Minister Barthou Tours Eastern Europe, Austrian Chancellor Flies to Budapest for the Second Time 29

(London) French Foreign Minister Barthou departed today for the capitals of Romania and Yugoslavia to consolidate France's Eastern Alliance. The issues he will discuss with the two countries will be the same as those discussed by the leaders of Italy and Germany in Venice recently. Barthou's trip is a result of his recent visit to Warsaw. Before his departure, Barthou publicly denied that France intends to encircle Germany. However, there is no doubt that France wants to resist Germany's rearmament. Austrian Chancellor Dollfuss also flew from Vienna to Budapest. Rumors spread that Dollfuss may visit Italian Prime Minister Mussolini again.

Hitler's special envoy for disarmament, Ribbentrop, recently went to London and has now arrived in France, where he was cordially received by French Prime Minister Doumergue. The two had a brief discussion, but the results are unknown.

Hitler's speech in Gera yesterday directly attacked alliances and blocs. People in Berlin believe that Hitler's remarks have dashed Germany's hopes of returning to Geneva before its demands are recognized by all. (Reuters Telegram, 18th)

(Paris) Foreign Minister Barthou departed for the capital of Romania this evening to consult with the Romanian authorities. He is scheduled to stay for two days. Barthou's visit to Romania at this time is considered to be quite significant. (Havas Telegram, 18th)

(Havas Telegram, 18th)

Mussolini and Hitler Aim to Maintain the Balance of Power 30

Today, the Italian newspaper "Il Popolo d'Italia" in Rome published a lengthy article on the recent meeting between Hitler and Mussolini. The newspaper stated that during the discussions between the two leaders, there was no suggestion of concluding a separate treaty. The purpose of their meeting was not to drastically alter the map of Europe. The primary objective was to consolidate and ensure lasting peace in Europe. Mussolini's desire for peace is well-known, and Hitler has repeatedly stated Germany's permanent renunciation of Alsace-Lorraine and Polish Silesia, which proves Germany's intention for peace. Furthermore, the two countries' equal opposition to governments of collusion between nations is also a manifestation of their desire for peace. On the other hand, both Germany and Italy have recognized that the re-establishment of a fundamental balance in Europe is an urgent matter, and the establishment of a fundamental balance requires the firm recognition of the rights of all countries. Regarding disarmament, the newspaper stated that Germany's attitude is clear: it will not return to Geneva until equal rights are established. The newspaper continued, "Among the major issues of establishing European equilibrium and cooperating with Germany, the Soviet Russian issue is the most important. Relations between Germany and Russia are currently extremely cold." To limit this coldness, the Soviet Union, after the Venice meeting between Hitler and Mussolini, sent a proposal to Berlin to conclude an Eastern Locarno Treaty, requesting that Germany, Poland, and Czechoslovakia join at the same time. Germany immediately rejected this proposal. This fact is unrelated to German-Soviet harmony but is a resistance to a collusive government. The restoration of relations and the avoidance of disputes between Germany and Russia are urgently needed to maintain peace in Europe." (National Telegram, 18th)

(New York) The New York Times published an editorial commenting on the meeting between Hitler and Mussolini, stating that "The comments of Italian newspapers show that Mussolini is somewhat disappointed with Hitler's excessive idealism and lack of understanding of European realities. The Italian Prime Minister himself is a highly pragmatic person. Therefore, Italian newspapers do not believe that Mussolini can approve of a National Socialist Party member as the Prime Minister of Austria, because the impractical National Socialist Party's rule over Austria is unlikely to be endorsed by the pragmatic Mussolini." The New York Times described the recent speeches given by the Italian Prime Minister in St. Mark's Square and by the German Chancellor Hitler in Gera. The Italian Prime Minister urged the Italian people to make further sacrifices to defend their country and prevent invasion, while Hitler also advised the German people to make further sacrifices to maintain the National Socialist Party's politics so that it can endure. The New York Times said that such similar speeches must be welcomed by the self-respecting German people. Recently, Germany's suspension of foreign debt payments has caused opposition from Britain, France, and other countries, leading to criticism of Germany for poor financial management, which is a gift from Hitler. No matter how well German newspapers propagandize, they cannot completely hide the facts from the German people regarding the criticism of Germany's debt reliance. Now, hearing the Italian Prime Minister and the German Chancellor make similar statements, the German people can at least comfort themselves. After Germany suspended foreign debt payments, the U.S. Ambassador to Germany officially protested to the German government, stating that its treatment of U.S. bondholders was inappropriate. The suspension of foreign debt payments, as a whole, is a severe lesson for Germany. For Hitler's sake, instead of dreaming of modifying the borders of other countries and world alliances, it is better to concentrate on managing its internal affairs." (Havas, 18th)

German Deputy Chancellor's Criticism of the National Socialist Party System Attracts National Attention 31

(Berlin) German Deputy Chancellor von Papen's extremely courageous public criticism of the National Socialist Party system at the University of Marburg has attracted national attention. Propaganda Minister Dr. Goebbels, after returning from Warsaw, immediately ordered the ban on the publication of Papen's speech. The first edition of today's Frankfurter Zeitung, which carried the speech, has been confiscated. (Reuters, 18th)

German Deputy Chancellor von Papen, at the University of Marburg here, delivered a speech on domestic policy issues, criticizing the current German system, which is quite noteworthy. Papen first praised Chancellor Hitler and his accomplishments, and then stated that at this crucial juncture, brave and loyal words are the responsibility that should be borne for the German revolution. Unfortunately, most German newspapers are unable to bear this responsibility at present. Papen also said that the current German government is fully powerful and strong. Appropriate and loyal criticism should not hinder the authority of the government. However, it is a pity that the general revolutionary youth regard those conservative elements who conscientiously fulfill their critical responsibilities as reactionaries. The reason why a one-party system is necessary is that it is sufficient to change the original system. If the system has been changed, and emerging superior elements have taken up important positions, then the existence of a one-party system is not essential. Referring to the division of religious factions in Germany, Papen asked those who advocate unification in Germany to think again. It must be known that Christian doctrine is the potential force of all Western thought. Will Germany be a new Germany of Christianity, or will it perish by indulging in the idealism of false religions? This depends on a firm struggle to determine. The German people have no right to transcend all Christian people. If so, the cultural trend is different from the daily experience of the German revolution, but at present, there is a mixture of the two. It is a slander to believe that culturalism is spiritual life. It is not only that the criteria for judging with human freedom and equality are the original concepts of Christianity and the 日　　nation, which is by no means a manifestation of liberalism, because justice is the basis of the country. In addition, Papen also criticized the false concept of worshiping figures. In conclusion, he said that we should not regard all criticisms as malicious, and we should not regard the dispirited and disappointed patriots as enemies of the country. If not, the future of the country will suffer major sacrifices. (Havas, 17th)

(Berlin) Deputy Chancellor von Papen delivered a speech on domestic policy issues at the University of Marburg yesterday, criticizing German domestic policy. This incident has aroused a strong impression in political circles. The government has ordered the press not to publish Papen's speech. People have made various speculations about Papen's speech, some saying that Papen warned against certain members of the National Socialist Party being too radical, and others saying that Propaganda Minister Goebbels' extreme National Socialism has aroused concerns among conservatives. Papen's speech is tantamount to challenging Goebbels. In short, Papen's publicly expressed views can at least be regarded as increasingly distant from the trends of the leaders of the National Socialist Party. Papen has a close relationship with Hitler, but now he is criticizing National Socialism so much, which is unprecedented. Some people say that a serious conflict has occurred within the German government, which is by no means true. However, it is indeed a fact that the unity of the German government is becoming increasingly disintegrated. Therefore, we should pay attention to the evolution of German domestic policy. Even if the current tense situation temporarily subsides, Papen's speech shows that there are two opposing theories in the National Socialist Party government. We should always pay attention to this situation. (Havas, 19th)

French Communist Party Riot Engages in Fierce Fighting with Police Overnight, Resulting in Forty Casualties on Both Sides 32

(Paris) The Communist Party rioted again in Toulouse last night. The street fighting in the city only stopped this morning. The intensity of the battle is reminiscent of the Paris riots in February. This riot is no different from ordinary riots. The cause of the riot was that the Communist Party intended to hold retaliatory demonstrations and planned to break into the meeting place of the opposition party, but was blocked by the police. The Communist Party then used its terror tactics, and none of the windows of nearby shops were spared. Furniture was stolen, cars were overturned, and the Communist Party then attacked the police's tanks. Two police patrol cars were also overturned and burned. The Communist Party fought more and more fiercely, throwing torches. The cavalry and police who came in a steady stream seemed to be able to control the overall situation at times. They planned to occupy the city center in the dark and set up obstacles. The Communist Party also attacked the police with bricks and pistols. By one o'clock in the middle of the night, a total of forty people were injured and twenty people were arrested. The riots were still in progress this morning. (National Telegram, 19th)

British and Russian Diplomatic Maneuvering Towards Turkey 33

(London) Before the meeting of the Steering Committee of the last Disarmament Conference in Geneva, it was rumored that Turkey would raise the demand to revise the 1923 Treaty of Lausanne, according to which military equipment could not be set up on both sides of the Dardanelles Strait. Now Turkey intends to request the cancellation of this provision so that it can reinstall defensive works. In early June, Turkish Foreign Minister Rüştü met with British Foreign Secretary Simon several times in Geneva, and it was heard that he had abandoned the previous proposal and no longer made the above request. Recently, the Daily Telegraph reported that Soviet Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov was greatly disappointed when he heard that the Turkish Foreign Minister had canceled the previous proposal. The reason is that Litvinov's original plan was to contain Britain in two steps: first, the Soviet Union would conclude a Mediterranean naval convention with other countries, and second, it would revise the treaty restricting military equipment in the straits. However, the Soviet Union's (diplomatic buying behavior) trick, wanting to make Turkey fall into its trap to plot against Britain, was rejected by Turkey. The relations between Britain and Turkey are very good. If Turkey is fooled, it will damage the friendly relations between Britain and Turkey. People generally approve of Turkey's attitude in this matter. (Havas, 19th)

Germany Suspends Debt Payments, the United States Protests 34

(Washington) The State Department today instructed U.S. Ambassador Dodd in Germany to protest certain measures taken by Germany to suspend debt payments, claiming that these measures are detrimental to U.S. bondholders. Ambassador Dodd was ordered to notify the German government, stating that the United States cannot approve of Germany's poor treatment of U.S. bondholders. According to today's news, German Ambassador to the United States Luther will soon return to his country to report to the government on the U.S.-German business negotiations. These negotiations are roughly conducted in accordance with the U.S.'s recently passed reciprocal tariff measures. It is said that Ambassador Luther also has a report on (a certain economic situation). According to the German government's notice to the United States on March 31, it could not repay the due war debt of 50 million yuan, but the due interest of 1.2 million yuan would be paid as scheduled three days later. At that time, Prime Minister Hull stated to German Ambassador Luther that the U.S. government had no right to change the debt terms, saying that this matter must be voted on by Congress. Today, Congress's attitude towards Germany has been determined, that is, if Germany does not pay this debt, the United States will also stop paying for the wartime losses that should be compensated to the German people. (National Telegram, 18th)

(London) Today, the London Times published a Washington communication, stating the opinions of U.S. officials on the recent proposal by the British Chancellor of the Exchequer to establish a clearing house between Britain and Germany. The communication said that after Germany's suspension of indemnity clearance, European creditor countries rose up to criticize, but this state of chaos has also aroused considerable resentment in the United States, because European creditor countries, on the one hand, condemned Germany's disregard for credit and delayed debt payments, and on the other hand, refused to pay the due U.S. war debts for the same reason. The United States has no plans for coercive or retaliatory actions against Germany, but if the establishment of a clearing house between Britain and Germany is detrimental to the United States, the United States will inevitably have to protest to London through normal diplomatic channels. The police should strictly search for him and ask the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for assistance. The 73rd U.S. Congress Adjourns Indefinitely, Granting Roosevelt Broad Powers to Transform the Country's Economic Future 37

(Washington) The second session of the 73rd U.S. Congress was adjourned yesterday at midnight. The funds and powers granted to President Roosevelt by this Congress are unprecedented in scope. During the congressional recess, the President can transform the economic future of the United States according to his personal views. The Senate was originally scheduled to adjourn last Saturday, but because the agenda was not completed, it was postponed until 11:05 last night. Although the House of Representatives had completed its work long ago, it also adjourned indefinitely at 11:43 due to the Senate's affairs.

Establishment of Nine Important Bills 38

In addition to approving an unprecedented amount of 5.2 billion in appropriations, this session also passed many bills that have a significant impact on the lives and economy of the American people, regardless of gender, age, or social status. The most important ones include the following nine items:

(1) National Exchange Control Act, which stipulates that all public debt transactions are under the management of the federal government. (2) Reciprocal Tariff Act, which authorizes the President to directly conclude trade reciprocity treaties with various countries. (3) Gold Dollar Devaluation Act, which stipulates the method of dollar devaluation and allows the national gold reserves to be nationalized. (4) Silver Act, which stipulates that the national treasury reserves must be equal to 25% of the total value of the national currency. (5) Federal Telecommunications Act, which stipulates that all national telephones, telegraphs, and wireless radio are under central management and are handled by a special government department. (6) Air Mail Act, which stipulates air mail contracts and restrictions on subsidies. (7) Cotton Production Restriction Act, which stipulates the method of taxation for exceeding the limit. (8) Philippine Independence Act. (9) Vinson Naval Act, which allocates funds to expand the navy to the extent permitted by the treaty.

The Harmony of Deliberations is Unprecedented Before Congress adjourned, the last important bill that the industry had been waiting for for a long time was the housing improvement bill, which allocated 200 million yuan for the construction and improvement of residences. After a brief debate, it was passed. In addition, the Railway Labor Act, which stipulates that labor unions established by companies are illegal and guarantees the right of railway workers to negotiate with unions, was also sent to the White House for the President to sign. After all matters were completed, members of both houses gave farewell speeches. The harmonious atmosphere was rare in party parliaments. (National Telegram, 19th)

The Closing Ceremony Breaks the Old Tradition (Washington)

In the hours before Congress adjourned, the members were all happy, which was very different from the tense struggle a few days ago. When the House of Representatives discussed the joint review report of the two houses on housing cases, senators gathered in groups, chatting and laughing. Even political enemies were like friends. The many elegantly dressed female guests in the auditorium were especially a decoration of the happy situation. The House of Representatives finally decided not to hold the old tradition of parades at the closing ceremony, so only a military band played the national anthem at the midnight closing of Congress, and the closing ceremony was completed. (Reuters, 19th)

The Signing of the Silver Case is Suddenly Postponed (Washington) The White House announced tonight that President Roosevelt had signed the Silver Act, but after an hour and a half, the press release was cancelled, claiming that it would be signed tomorrow night. As for the reason why the White House made this premature announcement and postponed the signing,

there is no way to find out. (National Telegram, 18th)

The Russian-Japanese Negotiations on the Incident of a Fake Ship Breaking into Russian Territorial Waters 39

(Moscow) The following TASS news was published here: Soviet Consul General in Harbin, Slavsky, delivered a statement to (Manchukuo) Deputy Minister of Foreign Affairs, Shimamura, in response to the latter's explanation of the (Manchukuo) ship incident on the Heilongjiang River.

Japanese Note 40

On June 5, Japanese Ambassador to Russia Ota submitted a note to Soviet Deputy Foreign Commissar Stomonyakov on this matter. In the note, Ota opposed Slavsky's statement, citing his statement during his conversation with Stomonyakov on May 22. The statement said that the DeCheng ship's approach to the Soviet riverbank was due to the ship being shot by bandits from the Manchurian riverbank. At the same time, Ota pointed out that during his conversation with Stomonyakov, he said that "when the (Manchukuo) ship was dodging the bandits' attack and retreating to the Soviet territorial waters, it was shot at by the Soviet riverside." This conversation is true. Ota added that his conversations on this issue did not involve deaths or injuries, while the statement of the (Manchukuo) diplomatic representative stated that "this death was the result of the Soviet riverside shooting." Ota believed that this part of his conversation with Deputy Foreign Commissar Stomonyakov on May 22 had been misused. He also expressed his concerns (that this would create a wrong impression on the general public) and requested that appropriate steps be taken. Ota reiterated that he did not object to the publication of this note.

Soviet Text 41

On June 10, Stomonyakov issued a note in response to the Japanese ambassador's note. (I only received a copy of the note No. 112 of June 5 on June 7, and I was shocked to read its contents.) The communiqué of the Soviet Consul General in Harbin's oral protest to the (Manchukuo) Deputy Minister of Foreign Affairs published in the newspapers on June 4 clearly did not have any statement that would allow us to conclude that anyone's opinion that the DeCheng ship was shot by the Manchukuo riverbank, resulting in the death and injury of several people on board, was Your Excellency's opinion. In fact, the only thing Your Excellency talked about in the statement by the Soviet Consul General in Harbin was this, that is, according to your statement to me on May 22, the DeCheng ship's approach to the Soviet riverbank was caused by being shot by bandits from the Manchukuo riverbank. In the note of June 5, Your Excellency reiterated the main purpose of Your Excellency's statement on May 22, but there is still something unclear, that is, which statement in the statement of the Soviet Consul General in Harbin (to the (Manchukuo) Minister of Foreign Affairs) does Your Excellency wish to correct, and which does Your Excellency wish to deny?

(Finally, Your Excellency is very dissatisfied with the fact that the Diplomatic Committee instructed the Soviet Consul General in Harbin to quote Your Excellency's statement. I do not want to elaborate on the criticism of this quote in Your Excellency's note, but I must tell Your Excellency that our conversation on May 22 was not a private conversation and had no confidential nature. At the same time, Your Excellency gave me this incident on the DeCheng ship, which is the current tense situation in the Far East, (this is Your Excellency's opinion), and did not make such reservations that Your Excellency's report cannot be quoted even when making statements to third parties.

(In Your Excellency's note of June 5, he also expressed displeasure with the fact that the newspapers published a statement quoting certain sentences Your Excellency made in our conversation on May 22. Here I should forgive myself for reminding Your Excellency of the following facts, that is, the main content of this conversation has been published in detail by the Tokyo newspapers, and quoted the report of the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs representative. Unfortunately, the content of the May 22 conversation recorded by the Tokyo newspapers is very inaccurate and erroneous. Not only are the points I have stated distorted in tone and content, but also Your Excellency has never said it, and it is also referred to as Your Excellency's statement. For example, the (Japanese Daily News) published on May 26 that a Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs spokesman said that when we talked on May 22, Your Excellency gave me a memorandum, which contained (The Soviet authorities' attitude towards the Japanese consulates in Blagoveshchensk and Khabarovsk is brutal and dishonest). I don't need to tell Your Excellency that this news is purely fabricated, and at the same time, there is no reason in the memorandum to produce this news. Japanese public opinion's information on diplomatic negotiations is inexcusable, and at the same time, it can never be a method to promote healthy relations between the two countries. I hope Your Excellency agrees with this point. In the past, the Tokyo newspapers have always reported inaccurately on certain issues discussed and the diplomatic negotiations conducted by our two countries' representatives. My predecessor, Sokolnikov, has repeatedly urged Your Excellency to pay attention to this. At this moment, I am again asking Your Excellency to take effective steps to stop these actions, because it is clearly detrimental to our two countries' friendship.)

(As for Your Excellency's desire to publish a denial in the note of June 5, or to publish the full text of Your Excellency's note, but from the above points of view, I really don't know what the object of the denial is, and I don't know what the reason for the publication is. However, if Your Excellency renews the request after receiving this note, I will ask the media in my country to publish Your Excellency's note. However, at that time, they will also publish my reply.)

After this note was issued, the Japanese side did not request that Ota's note of June 5 be published in the Soviet newspapers. However, on June 11, the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs published its note in the Japanese newspapers, and the Japanese newspapers did not publish Stomonyakov's reply, and there was no news about the fact that the Japanese ambassador received this reply. (TASS, 18th)

Case of the Robbery of the Shuntian Steamer: Qingdao Fleet Ordered to Set Sail 46

(Tianjin) The British Taikoo Company's Shuntian steamer departed from Tanggu at 3 PM on the 17th, loaded with passengers and cargo for export. At 6:30 PM, 180 li outside Dagu, a large group of dozens of sea bandits suddenly emerged from the lower deck, holding guns and restraining the chief officer and chief engineer. They dropped anchor in the sea, carried out a search, and gathered all valuables together. They also kidnapped five Western passengers, including a Japanese man named Yamamoto, two British soldiers, Mr. Nickell, the general manager of the British Manufacturers Life Insurance Company in Shanghai, and more than twenty Chinese people. At 8 PM, some sea bandits arrived in a sailboat, disembarked, and fled. Before leaving, they destroyed the ship's radio station and equipment, preventing the ship from sending out distress signals. On the 18th, after repairs, the ship barely managed to sail to Yantai and reported to the British and American navies, requesting them to send warships for suppression. (Special Telegram, 19th)

(Beiping) A foreigner in Beiping received a telegram from the British consulates in Tianjin and Yantai stating that the British Taikoo Company's Xin Shuntian left Tanggu for Shanghai at 3 PM on the 18th. At about 4 AM on the 19th, while passing through the waters near Sang Island, a large number of pirates were suddenly discovered on the ship. They first fired three blank shots as a warning, and at the same time, divided into groups to monitor the passengers' movements. Another group of bandits, holding guns, went to the engine room and destroyed the radio. The ship's third officer, a British man, was shot by the bandits and was in critical condition. After everything was settled, they began searching and robbing. Finally, more than twenty Chinese male and female passengers, three Western passengers, three foreign officers of the ship, and one Japanese passenger were kidnapped and taken away on a small boat prepared in advance, riding the waves. The Xin Shuntian steamer arrived in Yantai this afternoon and has telegraphed Beijing and Shanghai for assistance. The Qingdao fleet has been ordered to set sail to patrol the location of the incident and suppress the pirates. (Special Telegram, 19th)

(Yantai) The sea bandits who robbed the Shuntian ship, besides searching and robbing the passengers' belongings, did not harass them. Yesterday afternoon at 5 PM, before leaving the ship, the bandits even treated the foreign passengers to coffee and pastries. The pirates kidnapped a total of twenty-six people, including twenty Chinese, five British, and one Japanese, named Yamamoto, who was said to be related to the Japanese army. There were also several American women among the passengers, but fortunately, none of them were kidnapped. Among the foreign passengers, besides the British, Americans, and the Japanese man Yamamoto, there were no other nationalities. The foreign passengers highly praised the captain, Christiansen, and other crew members, who, even in a very difficult situation, did their best to assist the passengers. The bandits apparently disguised themselves as passengers in Tanggu to board the ship. According to the wife of Mr. Houchong, the deputy manager of the Asia Petroleum Company's Tianjin branch, when the robbery occurred, she and her two children were fast asleep when they were suddenly awakened by gunfire. Then, they heard a lot of noise. Soon, several bandits entered the room and searched for money, clothing, and jewelry. Not long after, several female passengers and three children were confined by the bandits in the second-class dining room. They did not leave the room on Sunday. The bandits only chose strong young men to kidnap. Many passengers praised them. The Japanese man Yamamoto, who was kidnapped, was said to be related to the Tianjin Japanese army. However, his behavior was suspicious. His full name and other details are unknown. Yamamoto's ticket was purchased by a Japanese military officer named Nagura Tomo, through the Tianjin China Travel Service. Nagura wore Chinese clothing and stayed at the Beiyang Hotel with Yamamoto. According to the manager of the hotel, Nagura often stayed at the hotel and was said to be related to the Japanese army. This time, he used the name Zang Liansheng (transliteration) to register in the guest book. The hotel often bought tickets for Nagura to go to Tanggu, Tangshan, Shanhaiguan, and other places. On the day Yamamoto took the Shuntian steamer to Yantai, Nagura also went to Tangshan. When the Japanese authorities heard the news of the Japanese man Yamamoto's kidnapping, they immediately dispatched a cruiser from Dalian at full speed to Yantai, which arrived at the port at noon today. Among the kidnapped Chinese, there was Shen Tianlin (transliteration), who served as the Minister of Interior during Wu Peifu's administration. According to reliable sources, the mail and cargo carried by the Shuntian ship were not touched by the bandits. Reuters learned from reliable sources that the five civilian boats used by the bandits, two were registered in Yantai and three were registered in Tianjin. This afternoon at 5 PM, the condition of the Shuntian ship's third officer, Mr. Ross, has not changed. Mr. Ross is still lying in the hospital, receiving careful treatment from doctors. Shandong Chairman Han Fuqu has responded to the urgent telegram from the Chinese Commissioner of the Maritime Customs Service and dispatched a detachment of provincial troops from Wuding to Lijin, a county located about thirty miles inland from the mouth of the Yellow River, believing that the bandits are advancing towards the territory of Lijin County. According to reports, the foreign passengers kidnapped from the Shuntian ship, in addition to the Japanese Yamamoto, include Mr. Nicoll from Shanghai, British Naval Major Field, and Luce. The Shuntian ship's second officer, Brandt, age 27, and third-class engineer Watson, age 31. (Reuters Telegram, 19th)

(Yantai) The Shuntian ship, escorted by the British destroyer HMS Witch, arrived here at 5 AM this morning. The news of the ship's robbery spread throughout the area last night. Therefore, many foreigners, including some who were vacationing here, gathered at the pier at dawn to wait for the ship's arrival. Ross, who was injured on the ship, was treated by the British destroyer HMS Witch last night. Today, after the ship docked, with the assistance of the American naval personnel here, Ross was carried ashore and sent to the American hospital. Ross suffered a serious gunshot wound, but his condition is stable. Admiral Dreyer, Commander-in-Chief of the British Fleet in China, has telegraphed the American naval authorities here to thank them for the assistance provided to Ross by the American naval personnel. The foreign passengers on the Shuntian ship included five women, some children, and seven men. Mr. and Mrs. Lyle, the British Consul-General in Qingdao, were also among them. In addition, there was the Japanese man Yamamoto. According to the people on the ship, the women were all calm and brave. Mrs. Warren, Mrs. Learmouth, and Mrs. Lyle all locked themselves in their rooms. Although the bandits repeatedly shouted and demanded that they open the doors, they did not break out. Mrs. Houchong was especially calm. Captain Christiansen of the ship told a Reuters reporter that the incident occurred at 10:30 PM on Sunday. There were about thirty bandits in total, all carrying weapons. Several bandits first entered the radio room, captured the two operators, and imprisoned them in the smoking room. Mr. Christie heard a lot of noise outside and rushed out of his room to investigate. As soon as he left the room, he was captured by three armed bandits and also imprisoned in the smoking room. At that time, the helmsman was the third officer, Mr. Ross, who was attacked by the bandits and suffered a serious gunshot wound. Two other crew members and two engineers were also arrested at the same time and sent to the smoking room. Several bandits guarded them in that room until 5 PM on Sunday. During this time, the helmsman was the third pirate, who was obviously an experienced navigator and steered the ship towards the mouth of the Yellow River. There, five civilian boats were docked. It is not possible to determine whether they were in collusion with the pirates. However, in any case, these five boats were requisitioned by the pirates. The Shuntian ship ran aground on a soft sandbar. Fortunately, after the pirates left the ship on Sunday afternoon, the ship floated again. The pirates did not cause any physical damage to the ship, nor did they damage the radio. Therefore, a distress signal could still be sent out at 5:30 PM. The cargo on the ship was not taken by the pirates. However, the passengers' suitcases and luggage were all robbed. All clothes, jewelry, money, and valuables were looted. Even the jewelry worn by Mr. Houchong's children was robbed. The bandits took the opportunity to change into Chinese clothes and discard their original old clothes on the ship. Some of them wore a mixture of Chinese and Western clothes. They seemed particularly interested in eyeglasses. Several pirates told the Shuntian ship's comprador that they were Shandong smugglers and that because the customs inspection was too strict, they robbed the ship to retaliate, causing trouble for the government. Before leaving the ship, the pirates announced that they wanted to kidnap four foreign passengers and two crew members. The captain asked the pirates to draw lots to decide who to kidnap, but the pirates refused. They then chose Mr. Nicoll, Major Field, Major Luce, Mr. Yamamoto, and the crew members Brandt and Watson. After the ship ran aground at the mouth of the Yellow River, the above six foreigners were driven into a civilian boat. The pirates initially planned to kidnap the Shuntian's chief officer, but because the captain told them that he needed the chief officer to help him sail the ship, the pirates changed to kidnapping the second officer, Mr. Brandt. Not everyone on the ship was disturbed. The Shuntian ship's accountant slept soundly during the robbery. On Sunday, he got up and walked to the deck, thinking that the ship had arrived in Yantai. To his surprise, he was arrested by the pirates and locked in the smoking room. When the pirates occupied the Shuntian ship, two engineers were forced by the bandits at gunpoint to manage the engines as usual until 9 AM on Monday, when the pirates replaced them with two other engineers. There were eight pistols and four other types of guns on the ship, all of which were looted. (Reuters Telegram, 19th)

(Beiping) The British Embassy has made serious inquiries to the Central Government and Shandong Chairman Han Fuqu regarding the Shuntian steamer robbery. At the same time, they have dispatched Naval Attaché Duri to Jinan tonight to discuss with Han Fuqu the methods to rescue the kidnapped people. (Reuters Telegram, 19th)

(London) All newspapers have prominently featured the news of the Shuntian steamer robbery. The general opinion is that this case will not seriously affect Sino-British relations. London newspapers today praised the abilities of Shandong Chairman Han Fuqu and expressed confidence that Mr. Han will be able to make efforts to rescue the kidnapped people. The pirates claimed that they were originally smugglers and that recently, because the customs authorities have dispatched many patrol boats to various places along the Shandong coast to crack down on smuggling, they committed this robbery to retaliate. This statement has attracted much attention from merchants here. British merchants have repeatedly complained about the excessively high Chinese tax rates and will now try to persuade the government to inform the Chinese government about the adverse effects of excessively high tax rates on all countries, both Chinese and foreign. (Reuters Telegram, 19th)

Victory Report on Bandit Suppression in Jiangxi Province 50

(Nanchang) Xiao Ke, the bandit leader on the west bank of the Gan River, used Jinhua Mountain as his lair. Yesterday, it was bombed by the Lotus Garrison. Six bombs were dropped on the bandit fortifications and trenches in the first attack. The bandits fled into the mountains to the northeast. Another bomb was dropped on the bandits, and it exploded in the middle of them. Four bombs were dropped in the second attack, one hitting a sentry post and three hitting trenches. In the third attack, seeing no bandits in the fortifications, only scattered bandits hiding in the woods, two bombs were dropped, both exploding in the middle of them. The two bandit leaders, Xiao Ke and Cai Huiwen, held a pseudo-military conference in Piaofang. Xiao advocated defending the old Jiangxi lair, while Cai advocated seeking other activities. They argued and pointed guns at each other. The pseudo-political director, Yu Zhaolin, mediated and warned each other. (Special Telegram, 19th)

(Nanchang) Liu Jianxu reported on the 19th that Ge Yong, the chief of staff of the pseudo-Hunan-Jiangxi Military Region, confessed that (1) the pseudo-Hunan-Jiangxi Military Region needs 50,000 yuan in military expenses per month, all of which depends on squeezing rice, issuing pseudo-public bonds, and confiscating and looting. Bandit soldiers eat only two meals of thin porridge a day. (2) Regardless of gender, those aged 16 to 20 in the bandit area are organized into Young Pioneers, and those under 50 are organized into Red Guards. This kind of oppression forces them to be drafted into Red Guard militias, which are then concentrated and reorganized into the Red Army. The bandits are now implementing compulsory military service, forcibly conscripting them. After the recovery of the Zixi area, the old lair of the Fang bandits on the south bank of Qianshan, a certain unit more than ten miles above the bandit-occupied area is advancing to the Fujian border, which will be fully recovered. The HeKou disaster relief center has been advanced to Hengfeng. Moreover, the victims of Shangrao, under the cover of the volunteer army, are searching for food in the bandit area, while the old and weak are left behind to cultivate the land. (Special Telegram, 19th)

Bandit Xu retreated and gathered at Zhengjiafang, constructing fortifications to resist. On the morning of the 18th, Yu personally led the regiments in a fierce attack. After four hours of intense fighting, Zhengjiafang was finally recaptured, and aftermath management is being handled. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 19th)

Chiang Orders Provinces to Reduce Additional Land Tax 丨Five Provinces Including Hubei and Hebei Have Already Replied丨 89

Nanchang Correspondence: In order to reduce the burden on farmers, Chairman Chiang, based on the resolutions of the Ten-Province Grain Conference, telegraphed all provinces from the Field Headquarters, instructing them to thoroughly investigate and list additional land taxes for examination, and to report the reduction of additional tax rates. The provinces and cities that have already replied include Hubei, Hebei, Anhui, Henan, Jiangxi, and the Shanghai Special Municipal Government, reporting the amount of additional land tax and the reduction situation in their respective provinces and cities. Chiang individually instructed and informed them. The remaining provinces are still complying. The brief situation of the reports from each province and Chiang's instructions are recorded below:

Hubei: The Director of the Hubei Finance Department replied that Hubei is a bandit suppression area, and the necessary security team's salaries and provisions are still designated to be funded by the mu tax as the basic expenditure. The mu tax is temporary in nature and will be abolished after the banditry is pacified. The Field Headquarters instructed that this was not allowed, stating roughly: Upon review, the land tax should collect more than 1.608 million yuan in additional taxes from various provincial tax items, which is the part attached to the regular tax. In addition, the provincial Ding Cao additional tax, together with the county local additional tax levied from the county tax items, and the mu tax amount to more than 5.141 million yuan, which belongs to the additional tax part. The ratio of additional tax to regular tax is almost equal to twice the regular tax, which is not in line with the established case that the additional tax should not exceed the regular tax. As for the mu tax, if it is mostly collected along with the grain, it is also one of the additional taxes and cannot be considered different from the additional tax simply because it is collected temporarily. Moreover, the province has a vast area and fertile land, but the amount of land tax collected is only more than 2.608 million yuan, which inevitably has the drawback of little grain and much land. You should immediately supervise the relevant authorities to thoroughly organize and report for verification in order to gradually align with the principle of balanced taxation, which is of utmost importance, and so on.

Hebei: Hebei only submitted a list of counties with additional land taxes that have been collected and those that have not. Chiang instructed: Upon review, the additional land tax in 41 counties such as Cangxian and Nanpi exceeds the regular tax by more than one time, and the additional tax in counties such as Jiahe, Jingxian, Wuqiao, Dongguang, and Wen'an exceeds the regular tax by more than three times, which is too harsh and complicated. You should immediately supervise the relevant authorities to follow the regulations promulgated by the Ministry for the reorganization of additional land taxes, and promptly reorganize and verify the reductions. In addition, the land where additional taxes are not levied in the province should also be listed separately as a basis for assessing the total amount of land tax in the province, and should be investigated and supplemented after the reorganization and reduction of additional donations.

Anhui: Anhui's reply telegram also stated that the additional taxes in various counties have increased due to the urgent need for funds for the bandit suppression teams, and measures are being drafted to reduce them. The Field Headquarters instructed five points: (1) Upon review, the additional land tax in counties such as Lujiang and Lu'an exceeds more than twice the regular tax, and there are many other counties that exceed one to two times. You should immediately follow the regulations promulgated by the Ministry for the reorganization of additional land taxes and thoroughly reduce them. (2, 3, 4 omitted) (5) The province has jurisdiction over 61 counties. What is the total amount of land tax in each county? The table did not include it. A detailed table should be reported after the additional reduction.

Henan: The Henan Finance Department replied: (1) The actual Ding Fu additional tax in each county does not exceed the regular tax. (2) In counties with less Ding silver, the mu tax inevitably exceeds the regular tax. (3) Recently, due to the expansion of security teams for bandit suppression, the additional taxes in each county in the province almost all exceed the regular tax. If the reduction is carried out in accordance with the regulations promulgated by the Ministry, it will be difficult for each county. The Field Headquarters instructed that the reduction of additional land tax is a general case. You should immediately supervise the relevant departments to draft a specific reduction plan based on the actual situation of each county and submit it for further review. Jiangxi: Due to the previous county autonomy and the urgent need for bandit suppression, the additional land tax in Jiangxi province has accumulated to the present day. Those with high taxes exceed the regular tax by four or five times, and those with low taxes are one or two times. They have now followed the regulations and uniformly reduced them to less than 70%, with an annual reduction of approximately two to three hundred thousand yuan, which has been reported to the Field Headquarters for record.

Shanghai: The Shanghai Special Municipal Government replied that since the division of the city and county in the 17th year, they have collected taxes in accordance with the old tax rules without any additional fees. However, in the Jiading Mountain area, some additional donations slightly exceeded the regular tax by about one li of silver, but the number is very small, and the rest are lower than the regular tax. (14th)

Remnants of the Communists Differ on Escape and Defense, Food, Salt, Ammunition, and Medicine in the Communist Areas Are Exhausted, Main Force and Elite Are Almost Completely Lost 90

Shantou Correspondence: The military affairs of bandit suppression on the border of Fujian, Guangdong, and Jiangxi provinces have taken on a new form since Chiang Po-cheng arrived in Guangdong. Li Yang, commander of the Second Column, has remained in the province to await the outcome of military strategy discussions. The Eighth Division, led by Huang Zhiwen, captured 27 people, including Chen Kezhong, chairman of the Jiangnan County Soviet and important members of the Communist Party, in the battle of Junmen. After being interrogated and verified by the Third Army Department in Meixian, He Guanfang Lian was specially dispatched to escort Chen Kezhong and others to Shantou, where they were transferred to the Fu'an warship and escorted to the province. According to the confessions of the Communist bandit leaders, the Communist bandits in Jiangxi are surrounded by the National Army and have fallen into a state of siege. Those who are employed only receive one meal and one bowl of porridge a day. Salaries have been suspended since May of last year, and it has been a year now. The official allowance fee is 4 yuan per month for junior officers, 6 yuan for field officers, and 10 yuan for generals. The soldiers under their command have repeatedly mutinied, looting everywhere, and the officers cannot stop them. In fact, there is nothing to rob in the Communist areas. The young and strong people are scattered, and the old and weak die in the ditches. Due to the lack of salt, many suffer from beriberi. Recently, soldiers and civilians on the border of Fujian and Jiangxi have defected with their weapons, it is said.

Also, according to military reports from the front, the Communist bandit Luo Binghui's troops are currently stationed in Changting, Zhu De's troops are stationed in Gutian Shicheng, Ye Jianying's troops are stationed in Huichang, and Dong Zhentang and Xiao Ke's troops are stationed in Yudu Xingguo. The pseudo-17th Army Corps is in Liangxi Caoxieling (near Changting) on the border of Fujian and Jiangxi, and the pseudo-9th Army Corps is south of Guangchang. Bandit Ye once dispatched Communist bandits from Ruijin Huichang to station at Shuikou, Jiangtou, Baibu, Pingyan, and other places to strictly guard against the Huai attack by the Southern Route Army. According to what is heard here, the Communist bandits have differing opinions on escape and defense. Those who advocate escape want to flee to Sichuan and Guizhou to join Bandit Xu, while those who advocate defense believe that if they abandon their nests and flee elsewhere, they will inevitably be intercepted and annihilated along the way. The Communist leaders have different wills, and the hearts of the people are shaken. The sign of a total collapse is fully revealed.

Also, it is reported that after the Communist bandits were severely suppressed by the National Army five times, their elite troops were almost completely lost. Currently, each division is less than one regiment, and each regiment is smaller than a battalion of the National Army. The pseudo-22nd Division, which was stationed in Junmen and was known for its ferocity, was defeated in Junmen, and the division commander was sent to Huichang for punishment. Last month, the remnants of the division invaded Luotian and were defeated again by the bandit suppression group. They retreated to Huichang. On the 2nd of this month, they attacked Chongshi Tianxin in Anyuan and were defeated again by Li Zhen's regiment. Only five or six hundred people escaped. Now the division has been completely annihilated, and the name of the division no longer exists. In Huichang City, there are only thousands of student soldiers, model divisions, worker-peasant soldiers, and red guards newly transferred from Ruijin. Because of the disappearance of its strength, the Communist bandits forced the people in the Communist areas to become soldiers. Gu Longchang, the pseudo-Soviet chairman of Xunwu Anyuan County, opposed the conscription of those over 40 years old. When the Eighth Division conquered Qingxi, Gu was unwilling to lead the masses to flee with the Communist army, which led to his killing by the Communist bandits. Many people in Qingxi and Luotian were killed by the Communist bandits. Now the people in these two places are fleeing one after another. The National Army has established a temporary post-disaster relief association to accommodate them and organized a 500-member bandit suppression group under the command of Ouyang Xin, the magistrate of Huichang County, in order to assist the National Army in eliminating the bandits.

(14th)

Yuping Road to Start Construction Soon, Yunan Section Divided into Four Sections, Inviting Merchants to Bid for Construction Projects 91

Zhou Correspondence: After the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway was ordered to be renamed the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway, the Railway Engineering Bureau immediately formed surveying teams and drilling teams to set off one after another. Except for the Yushan-Nanchang section, which has been surveyed, the Shangrao-Guixi section is still being rushed to survey the route on the north bank of the Xinhe River. The other lines have been basically determined, and the entire section has been divided. The entire section from Yushan to Nanchang is divided into four sections, and each section is divided into four segments. The first section starts from Yushan Station to Shaxi in Shangrao County. The second section is from Shaxi to Shangrao County. The third and fourth sections and the fifth, sixth, seventh, and eighth sections of the second section are still being surveyed. After the line is determined, it will be divided again. The third section starts from Taiqiao Chenjia in Guixi County to Zongmaogang in Guixi County as the ninth section. From Zongmaogang to Yangxi Chenjia in Dongxiang County as the tenth section. From Yangxi Chenjia to Siqian in Dongxiang County as the eleventh section. From Siqian to Xiabuji in Jinxian County as the thirteenth section. The fourth section is from Xiabuji to Gaoqiao in Jinxian County as the thirteenth section. From Gaoqiao to Liangjiadu in Nanchang County as the fourteenth section. From Liangjiadu to Liantang in Nanchang County as the fifteenth section. From Liantang to Nanchang as the sixteenth section. Each section of 10,000 cubic meters of engineering work is being put out for tender and construction, and the bidding will be opened on the 25th of this month, and contracts will be awarded separately, and construction will begin simultaneously. Regarding the improvement along the line, after Deputy Director of the Bureau Hou Jiayuan inspected, he believed that the various business equipment of the Jinyu branch were not perfect, and he planned to supplement them immediately. He also sent Deputy Engineer Chen Zujun to inspect the bridge engineering of the Pinghan and Longhai Railways to learn from them. All freight warehouses, rain sheds, station platforms, and other projects in each station will be built quickly. In addition, the tasks such as transferring road police for training and studying and promoting business methods are being carried out separately. (June 17)

Suzhou, Chen Yu to Be Escorted to Zhenjiang for Investigation 92

Chen Yu, the chairman of the Garment Industry Guild, was arrested during the strike of garment industry workers on suspicion of being a member of the Axe Gang and has been detained in the Public Security Bureau for more than ten days and has not been released. Chen accused Shen Wei, the director of the Public Security Bureau, of illegal arrest and filed a complaint with the local court against Shen for abuse of power and obstruction of freedom. After investigation by the prosecutor, it was deemed that Shen, as the director of the Public Security Bureau, arrested Chen to maintain local security during the strike, which was not improper, and the case was dismissed. On the one hand, the county government reported the situation to the Department of Civil Affairs for verification. Yesterday, it was instructed to escort Chen to Zhenjiang for investigation.

Tonglu Road Fire Burns Ten Homes 94

The Guangming Hospital on Tonghui Road in Xiyi was initially organized by doctors Jin Deming and others, and was taken over by Western medicine doctor Guo Songyi a week ago. Unexpectedly, at four o'clock the night before, a fire suddenly broke out on the floor of the hospital. At that time, the wind was raging and the fire was extremely fierce, turning into a prairie fire. It spread to the Xiangtai Grain Store on the right, as well as the Baohe Tang Chinese Medicine Store, Ding Yongtai Machine Wood Sample Shop, Yuantong Grocery Store, Tongyi Refined Salt Company, Chengcang Iron Factory, Dai Deyuan Iron Factory, Xinshunxing Iron Factory, Yidefeng Foreign Goods Store, Tianchang Tofu Store, and more than ten other stores. The fire lasted for two and a half hours, causing losses of 40,000 to 50,000 yuan. Only Tongyi Refined Salt Company had fire insurance of 10,000 yuan, and Baohe Tang Chinese Medicine Store had insurance of 2,000 yuan. The rest were not insured against fire. Afterwards, the Sixth Branch of the Public Security Bureau ordered Guo Songyi, who started the fire, and Xu Yinggong, the owner of Baohe Tang Medicine Store, to come to the bureau to inquire about the cause of the fire, and they were immediately released on bail. In addition, three firefighters, Sun Genquan, Zhang Liangfu, and Shen Quan, were injured during the firefighting and have been sent to the hospital for treatment.

Changshu, Road Workers on the Suzhou-Changshu Highway Petition 95

The County Government here received an order from the Department of Transportation that in order to prepare for the opening of the Transportation Fair, the Suzhou-Changshu Highway must be built and completed by the end of July. The county has now invited bids and signed a contract with Wang Ankang's workshop to build the road. Unexpectedly, when personnel from the Engineering Office of the County Construction Section set out to set stakes to prepare for construction the other day, they suddenly discovered that the flat plan approved by the Provincial Construction Department was different from the county's soil excavation survey. Therefore, they reported to the province for instructions on the one hand, and stopped construction on the other hand. However, after the road work was stopped, more than 1,000 workers who contracted to build the road had already come to Changshu. The sudden interruption of work and the loss to the road workers were huge. Wang Ankang's workshop specifically went to the county to petition, and declared the issue of responsibility, saying that the suspension of work for three days has already resulted in a loss of more than 3,000 yuan, which should be compensated by the county government, and so on.

Because of this, Pang Shoubai, the head of the Construction Section, went to the province in person because the matter was of great importance. He returned to Changshu on the 18th. According to reports, the contract signed between the county government and the workshop stipulated that construction would start on the 10th, and the road workers had already come to Changshu long ago. The county cannot be responsible for all the losses. The funds will be used to build the road mu tax, which should not be a problem. However, in order to alleviate the losses of the workers, in addition to telegraphing the Construction Department for instructions again, the construction of the ten meters on both sides of the bridge piers in each section will be started first to make up for it. As for the Changtai Road project, there are no obstacles and the progress is quite smooth. Construction has now started and it is expected that the entire road can be opened to traffic before the 20th of next month.

Changzhou, Locust Nymphs Everywhere on the Shores of West Lake 96

The farmland near the Dong'an Town in Wuyi Southern Township is mostly along the West Ge Lake. During the summer last year, a large number of flying locusts were discovered, and efforts were made to capture them day and night to avoid disaster. Unexpectedly, recently, locust nymphs have been found everywhere along the lake. Gu Zhizhuan, director of the Rural Improvement Experimental Zone there, went to conduct an on-site investigation and found that the larger locust nymphs had already grown wings and could fly, and the smaller ones were shaped like black ants and covered the fields. Director Gu immediately reported the situation to the county government for verification on the 18th. County Magistrate Cai immediately ordered the farm administrator He Zhaoxi to go to the countryside to guide the extermination and immediately...

Yangzhou, Xianzhen Breaks Large Batch of Bandit Suspects 97

Bandit cases have occurred frequently in Xiannv Town and Yiling in Yishui County. After the reconnaissance team arrested the bandit Gu Xiqing, he confessed to many accomplices. Gu was then taken as a spy and captured Gu Xie, Guan Guozaozi, Fang Guangcai, Xu Haichun, Zhu Wentao, Pan Xiaomazi, Yang Youyu, Qi Xiaosanzi, and other eight people in Xianzhen. Yantan Town, Robbery and Injury 98

Chen Shizhong, a resident of Yantan Town Xiye Chenzhuang in Jiangdu Fifth District, lived with Zhang Shiyi and Shirentong. He had more than 80 mu of land and was the wealthiest man in the area. He had long been coveted by bandits. Sun also took precautions in advance. In addition to digging two cellars in his house to store valuables and foreign currency, and receiving self-defense firearms and artillery, the entire courtyard of the house was covered with barbed wire, with only a narrow alley less than a foot wide uncovered. Unexpectedly, at dawn on the 17th, a few bandits with accents suddenly entered through the alley not covered with barbed wire, grabbed the entire family of Shizhong and bound them with nets, forcing them to hand over self-defense firearms, searching all the rooms for clothing and the foreign currency stored in the two cellars. They also used fire to burn and scorch the three brothers of Shizhong, forcing them to tell where the valuables were hidden until they were severely injured and on the verge of death. It is now reported that Shiyi was too seriously injured and died on the afternoon of the 17th. The local town Ding has reported to the town office and forwarded the report to the district for investigation. The total loss is said to be more than 3,000 yuan.

Haimen, Sea Bandits Rampant Along the Xun Tan Coast 99

Although the gang of sea bandits led by Pan Kaiqu was dispersed by the military and police in previous years, a part of them still appeared in the East China Sea and the East Ocean, robbing merchants and fishing boats. On the morning of the 11th, more than 100 bandits from the gang, driving five or six boats, landed in Xuntan, entered the village and kidnapped five people, including the resident Chen Dalang. Then they went to Sanzhuang Town and kidnapped seven fishermen, detained them on the bandit boat, and demanded a ransom of 300 to 400 or 500 to 600 yuan per person, with a strict deadline and threats to tear up the tickets if the deadline was missed. When the police and army heard the news and went to suppress them, the bandits had already set sail and fled. The local residents are now panicked. It is unknown how those responsible for maintaining security will find a way to resolve this situation.

The Situation of the Chunji Timber Firm Case in Qidong Is Suspicious 100

Ye Xian'gen, the owner of the Chunji Timber Firm in Lingjiang Port, has been in business for many years and has made a lot of profits. Last month, when he purchased a large batch of timber, the timber was scattered due to strong winds and high tides. The porters, Zhang Lang and others, rearranged them and transported them to the firm. By the evening, the porter Zhang Lang ran to the home of Huang Zhisan, who lived by the Jiangbin, claiming that his son, Xiaoyou, had once cut grass on the beach and stolen seven or eight large pieces of wood. They claimed to have been ordered by the owner to investigate and that you must go abroad to deal with it. Zhisan retorted that his son, Xiaoyou, was young and could not steal wood. Ten days later, the Chunji firm detained Huang's wife in the town, threatening her in every possible way. Xue Lao'er Xu Shouyi and others fined him 12 yuan. He paid 12 yuan immediately to escape temporarily. Afterwards, Zhisan, feeling unwilling, hired lawyer Huang to sue Xue and Xu for extorting money on the pretext of a problem. Xu and others, seeing that the case had expanded, detained Huang's wife at the Fourth District Office on the Dragon Boat Festival. On the other hand, they called the shop to carry three or four large pieces of wood into Huang's house in an attempt to cover up the truth.

Funing, Police Team Kills Notorious Bandit 101

Shi Ningtian, a notorious bandit in Lian and Fu counties, led his gang for several years, occupying Lian and Fu counties, burning, killing, and looting everything. The county government repeatedly issued orders to arrest him, but failed to do so. He also stubbornly resisted the police team from time to time. Unexpectedly, the bandit recently sneaked into Shenjiazhuang in Beixiang in our county, which was discovered by the police team. Huang Gongzheng, the captain of the Third Squadron of the Police Brigade stationed in Qitao, led the team to join forces with Wu Jianhong, a member of the guard regiment, and led the militiamen to encircle and suppress him. The bandit leader Shi Ningtian and Tian's uncle Sun Er were both killed on the spot, and Tian's brother Shi Baochang was captured. The rest all fled. The team has now sent the two bandit corpses and the captured bandit Shi Baochang to the city for verification by the county government.

Pinghu: Elementary School Teachers' Strike Creates Tense Atmosphere 102

Education Bureau Chief Huang Qingrui's relationship with the elementary schools in various districts has fractured due to the accumulation of unpaid education funds. After the County Education Association, along with the Education Associations of various districts, jointly issued a declaration stating their non-cooperation, Huang, misled by rumors, even submitted a written complaint to the County Magistrate. The complaint essentially stated that Mao Youlun, a teacher from one of the districts, was inciting all elementary schools to strike and requested action. Upon hearing this news, the elementary schools were furious, and a strike seemed imminent. The atmosphere suddenly became tense. County Magistrate Zhang urgently summoned representatives from each school to earnestly appease them and pledged to allocate funds to cover one month's worth of arrears, thus averting the action.

Ningbo: Fire at Datong River Road in Jiangdong 103

Yang Xiangmao Grocery Store, located at No. 36 Datong River Road in Jiangdong, suffered a fire yesterday (the 17th) at approximately 6:00 PM. The fire was caused by a careless apprentice who accidentally ignited a match while brewing tea. The fire quickly spread, breaking through the roof and extending to the neighboring Xianghe Clock Shop, Yuan Wanshun General Merchandise and Glass Shop, and residential buildings in the rear. Firefighters from various fire brigades rushed to the scene and extinguished the blaze after an hour of effort. The fire destroyed one and a half storefronts of Xiangmao, one and a half storefronts of Xianghe, one storefront of Yuan Wanshun, and two and a half residential buildings, resulting in a total loss of over 10,000 yuan. Yuan Wanshun and his tenants suffered the most significant losses.
