Western Woman Commits Suicide After Hearing of Daughter's Tragic Death 178

He Milasha Lai Bin (transliteration), a Western woman, 48 years old, lived alone in Shanghai at the front room on the third floor of 33 Fair Road. She had a daughter who lived in the United States. Recently, the woman suddenly received a letter stating that her daughter had died of illness in the United States. Upon hearing this bad news, the woman's nerves were immediately deranged, and she felt that she did not want to live. The day before yesterday, she suddenly had the idea of ending her life and secretly swallowed Werononal poison in her bedroom to commit suicide. She was discovered by a Russian woman living in the same building, Bo Linggai, who immediately reported it to the Huishan police station. After dispatching detectives to investigate, they found her lying on the sofa, already unconscious, and found a glass on her table with a small amount of remaining poison. She was immediately taken to Gongji Hospital for treatment but died. The body was taken to the Phelon Road Morgue. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court appointed Prosecutor Diao Chengtang, along with forensic doctor Zhang Yan, clerk Wang Zuji, and others, to visit the morgue to examine the body. After examining the body and hearing the testimony of Bo Linggai, Diao determined that the deceased He Milasha Lai Bin was female and had died from poisoning caused by taking Werononal. The body was handed over to her friend Ge Laobuwusi to claim the body and coffin.

The Public Works Department Plans to Improve the Conditions of Rickshaws 179

The Public Works Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council's Intelligence Office released a message stating that the department has decided that, starting from January 1st of next year, the maximum rickshaw rental fee will be limited to 80 cents of small silver currency. Compared to the current rental fee, this is a reduction of approximately 60 cents of small silver currency per day. At the same time, to facilitate implementation, it is decided that from August 1st of this year, the rental fee will first be changed to 100 cents of small silver currency, so that rickshaw owners can adapt in their business operations and fully comply with the conditions of the Public Works Department.

The Public Works Department has also adopted the recommendation of the Rickshaw Management Office to establish a Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Association. The association's finances will be kept independent, but it may also accept donations. At the beginning of its operation, the Public Works Department will appoint three directors (all serving without pay) to supervise the association's funds. These three directors will likely be the current members of the Management Office. In the future, the Public Works Department may reassign them at will. Under the directors, there will be an executive committee (also serving without pay), appointed by the directors, consisting of enthusiastic social workers who will be responsible for handling the association's affairs.

Membership in the Mutual Aid Association will be limited to public rickshaw pullers holding licenses. Once the association's operations can be carried out independently, rickshaw puller members will elect representatives to join the executive committee.

The general outline of the Mutual Aid Association's affairs includes: 1. Providing free medical services (diagnosis and care), either by establishing its own clinic or temporarily entrusting an existing hospital to handle it, with the association paying the fees. 2. Establishing bathhouses. 3. Establishing free dormitories or charging only low rents. 4. Providing education for members and their children. 5. Establishing cooperative stores. 6. Organizing entertainment such as movies. 7. Holding lectures on topics related to members' welfare and rickshaw services. 8. Other matters to be determined as needed.

The association's expenses will be funded by collecting half a small silver currency (5 cents) from each rickshaw shift. This amount will be collected by the rickshaw owners in addition to the rental fee stipulated by the Public Works Department. After being permitted to collect this fee, the rickshaw owners will pay $1.50 in silver currency per rickshaw per month to the Mutual Aid Association. When rickshaw owners apply for license renewal, they must have a receipt for this payment. The Public Works Department will give priority treatment to rickshaw owners who cooperate in granting licenses. This additional fee will be implemented when the rickshaw rental fee is reduced to 100 cents of small silver currency.

The initial work of the Mutual Aid Association will be to assist rickshaw pullers in obtaining rickshaw pulling licenses. In addition, at the beginning of operations, the association's funds may be used for other beneficial purposes. All association funds are purely for the welfare of rickshaw pullers and will not be used for other purposes.

After this plan is implemented, starting from August 1st of this year, rickshaw pullers will pay 100 cents of small silver currency for the rickshaw rental fee and an additional 10 cents of small silver currency as a donation, totaling 110 cents of small silver currency, which is a reduction of 30 cents compared to the current 140 cents. At the same time, rickshaw pullers can obtain all the benefits of the Mutual Aid Association.

Regarding the licensing of rickshaw pullers, the Public Works Department has already decided to instruct rickshaw owners to nominate four rickshaw pullers for each licensed rickshaw. However, the independence of the rickshaw pullers must be fully maintained, and they should also be allowed to apply for licenses directly from the Public Works Department. However, because rickshaw owners must entrust their property to the rickshaw pullers, and in order to ensure that the majority of those who pull rickshaws can still obtain licenses, it is appropriate for rickshaw owners to participate in the selection of rickshaw pullers. It is now decided to handle this in a compromise manner, with rickshaw owners recommending three names per rickshaw, and the remaining 10,000 licenses will be available for rickshaw pullers to apply for themselves.

The Management Office plans to set up rickshaw puller licensing offices in Zhabei (新閘) and Hongkou (虹口). As soon as the buildings are renovated, they will be opened, starting with the licensing of rickshaw pullers for private rickshaws. The Management Office has recently acquired inexpensive land in convenient locations for rickshaw pullers in order to build the Mutual Aid Association's buildings.

On the 15th of this month, the Management Office explained the Mutual Aid Association's plan to a major rickshaw owner in person. The Management Office intends to cooperate in good faith with the rickshaw owners' guild, if possible, in order to realize the reform. It originally intended to hold further talks with several other major rickshaw owners before announcing the Mutual Aid Association's plan. Unfortunately, the result of the talks on that day was the convening of a meeting of rickshaw owners, and at the meeting, the matter of additional donations was criticized as violating the interests of rickshaw pullers and was pointed to as a desire to use it to fund the Management Office. From the current explanation, it can be seen that the criticism is unfounded. However, during the talks on that day, the rickshaw owner strongly expressed his approval of the Mutual Aid Association's plan and, based on his personal business, expressed his willingness to cooperate with the Management Office to see it succeed.

In addition, the Public Works Department's Rickshaw Affairs Committee, due to its radical work, has aroused dissatisfaction among rickshaw merchants and rickshaw pullers regarding the procedures for changing rickshaw styles, collecting rickshaw puller relief funds, and issuing license certificates to rickshaw owners. Currently, more than 1,000 rickshaw owners in the Special District held an emergency general meeting at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and resolved to reject all suggestions and measures of the Public Works Department's Rickshaw Affairs Committee. At 3:00 PM yesterday, Yin Zhiling, Chairman of the Rickshaw Owners' General Meeting, met with Zhong, the Director-General of the Public Works Department, to report the dissatisfaction of the Rickshaw Owners' General Meeting with all the measures of the Public Works Department's Rickshaw Affairs Committee. Director-General Zhong expressed that although the Bureau had agreed to all the suggestions of the Rickshaw Affairs Committee, in order to take into account the impossible facts for rickshaw merchants, it had already been revised and would be announced soon, resolving to make the rickshaw pullers' relief association independent and not presided over by the Rickshaw Affairs Committee. Permission will be given for enthusiastic social figures to participate in mutual consultation and cooperation. The relief funds collected must not be used for the expenses of the Rickshaw Affairs Committee. All improved rickshaw styles should also be considered in light of the situation, and gradual changes should be made. Rickshaw merchants need not worry about immediately changing rickshaw styles. Although there are revisions to the rickshaw regulations, the general outline is not much different from the old regulations. It is hoped that you will pass this information on to the rickshaw merchants, reassure them, and not listen to rumors. Yin reported this to the directors of the Special District Rickshaw Merchants' Guild and special committee members that evening for discussion.

In addition, the Rickshaw Pullers' Relief Fund Committee held a meeting at the YMCA last night to send Cao Yunxiang to see the Rickshaw Affairs Committee to discuss the situation of rickshaw puller relief.

Yuan Tai Sen Paper Mill Resolves Labor Dispute 180

According to the Central News Agency, the Yuan Tai Paper Mill in Xujiahui, Jinyi Bridge, was originally founded by Cheng Linsheng, a prominent Shanghai merchant, and faced the Gen Tai Hehe Flour Mill from afar. The workers in both factories were recruited from the Cangzhou area of Hebei Province. Yuan Tai was established six or seven years ago and originally hired a Japanese engineer to preside over it. After the January 28th Incident, the foreman guided the shipment of goods. Due to poor management, it was intermittently shut down for more than a year, resulting in significant losses. Cheng had no intention of operating it, so he leased it to Liu Bosen, the owner of the Tianzhang Factory, to take over. After Liu took over, he hired a new foreman to recruit new workers. The old workers, who had been unemployed for a long time, were in an uproar. They asked their foreman, Liu Fuxin, to plead with the factory owner for reinstatement, but the factory owner refused. The old workers, with no means of living, were panic-stricken. On the one hand, they forced Liu Fuxin to find a way, and on the other hand, they directly requested from the factory, gathering at the factory gate. The factory then instructed the Public Security Bureau to send police to suppress them. Liu Fuxin again requested the help of the fellow villagers' association to mediate, but it was still unsuccessful. After the original factory owner interceded with the factory, and with the persuasion of Inspector Wang Yan, the opinions of both parties moved closer. Then, Zhao Nangong, Chairman of the Henan Fellow Villagers' Association, invited both parties to the association for formal consultation. The factory owner also sincerely persuaded the workers, and the opinions were completely eliminated. The method was drafted, and the factory made revisions. Both parties recognized it, and the mediation was signed on the spot, establishing the resolution peacefully after a nearly month-long turmoil. The conditions are recorded as follows: 1. The Senji Factory and the office will hire 15 people, and Tianzhang will hire 15 people. The wages will be determined by the employer, and the workers may not dispute them. 2. If the workers hired by Tianzhang do not violate the factory rules, the factory will maintain their work for one year. If they are indeed good and are dismissed by the factory owner, the factory owner will grant them wages for the remaining months, calculated according to one year, excluding the days already worked. 3. Senji is willing to pay $1,000 to Mr. Zhao Nangong of the Hebei Fellow Villagers' Association as travel expenses for 40 dismissed workers to return home. 4. If workers hired by Senji and Tianzhang commit violations of factory rules, the factory has the right to dismiss them at any time and is not responsible for the wages stipulated in Article 2. 5. The entire group should apologize to the factory and the injured workers. 6. The above mediation conditions are guaranteed by the Hebei Fellow Villagers' Association to be fulfilled.

The Railway Bureau Orders the Handling of Employee Performance Appraisals and Salary Increases This Year; Reports Are to Be Submitted to the Bureau Before July 10th to Serve as the Basis for Salary Increases and Disciplinary Action According to Regulations 181

The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration issued a decree to the offices and departments yesterday, stating, "The performance appraisal period for the first half of the 13th year of the Republic of China has arrived. Performance appraisal registers should be prepared immediately for employees who have been at their current grade or received a promotion for one year or more between January 1st and June 30th of this year, and their daily work performance, whether it is excellent, good, or has merits and demerits, should be stated fairly, with accurate comments added. These should be submitted to the Bureau before July 10th to serve as the basis for salary increases and disciplinary action according to regulations. (The salaries of technical personnel should be handled in accordance with the National Railway Technical Personnel Position and Salary Grade Job Description Comparison Table, and the salaries of other staff and clerks should be handled in accordance with the National Railway Bureau Staff Salary Grade Table. Those not listed in the salary grade table should be handled in accordance with the railway regulations.) In addition to distribution, you are hereby ordered to comply with this decree."

Xinwei Relief Society Sends Refugees to Various Places Yesterday; Allocates Various Medicines to Relieve Disaster Victims in Jiangsu and Anhui 182

Yesterday, ten refugees, including Mr. and Mrs. Li Ruan, originally from various places in Anhui, Hubei, and Jiangsu provinces, who were disaster victims who came to Shanghai last winter to beg for food and have been here for half a year, learned that their hometowns had all calmed down and wanted to return home, but were suffering from a lack of travel expenses. Yesterday, Mr. Li and others went to the Xinwei Relief Society in this port to state their situation and begged to be sent back to their hometowns so that they could make a living and avoid drifting in a foreign land for a long time. The society, based on the request, made inquiries one by one. Ge Junxun and Chen Hongyou, two directors, separately issued ten wheel tickets and ordered the servant to send them to the China Merchants Wharf, where they boarded a steamer at 8:00 AM yesterday morning to return to their hometowns.

In addition, the Jiangsu Second Prison, with thousands of prisoners, had a sudden outbreak of plague, and the weather was hot, so it requested the Xinwei Relief Society to allocate medicine for relief. Xu Xiangfu of the Anhui Civil Affairs Department also requested medicine for rescue. After receiving the letter, the Society allocated 200 bottles of summer heat medicine, 200 bottles of dysentery powder, 200 bottles of Jisheng pills, 200 bottles of seasonal epidemic water, 200 bags of noon tea, and 50 bags of malaria pills to the Second Prison. It also allocated more than 400 pieces of summer heat medicine, etc., to the Anhui Civil Affairs Department, all packed in boxes and sent separately.

Yifeng Lane Opens a Rent Reduction Meeting; It Is Resolved to Pay Rent at 70% of the General Association's Rate 183

Yifeng Lane, located on Zhifu Road, Guizhou Road, in the Public Concession, is owned by the Jewish Yifeng Foreign Firm and was built in 1932. The rent is higher than in other places, so there are many empty houses, and they have not been completely rented out to this day. The residents of the lane, due to the current commercial depression and economic exhaustion, have reduced both food and clothing expenses. However, the rent has not yet reached the goal of reduction. For this reason, they invited all the residents of the lane to hold a general meeting yesterday, and Yang Zhongfu was publicly elected as chairman. Ren Nongxuan was sent by the General Association for Rent Reduction to supervise, and Zheng Xiaolin was sent by the 35th District Branch to guide. The Case Against the Doctor at the Shangxian Church Women and Children's Hospital Was Adjudicated Yesterday; The Court Ruled That There Was No Negligence 184

Two years ago, Mrs. Shen Li had an abortion and suffered from continuous bleeding. She went to the hospital for treatment, and Dr. Zhu performed the operation, which resulted in a good outcome. Therefore, she still went to the hospital for childbirth this year. After the lady was admitted to the hospital, there was no sign of labor for six days, everything was normal, only that she had a slight water discharge at home. During this period, the cervix did not open, and there was no need for surgery. On the seventh day, she naturally went into labor, but the contractions were weak and the progress was slow. This day happened to be a Sunday, and there was only one doctor in the hospital, so Dr. Zhong, the original introducer, was invited to consult. After the research, it was not yet the time to perform surgery. The next day, Dr. Lan, Director of Obstetrics and Gynecology at the Red Cross General Hospital, was invited to come for a diagnosis in the morning. Dr. Lan believed that she could not start yet. It was not until 7:00 PM that Dr. Lan came again to perform the surgery himself. The surgery was very difficult. After the fetus was delivered, the placenta adhered to the uterine wall and could not come down on its own, so it had to be removed with surgery. However, after removal, the uterus contracted weakly, resulting in continuous bleeding. Gauze was used to fill it, and injections of uterine contraction drugs and cardiotonics, as well as saline, were all ineffective. This kind of postpartum hemorrhage was actually caused by weak uterine contraction, which led to death. Afterwards, her husband, Shen Wenda, was very sad, but he had no complaints against the doctor. Unexpectedly, a month later, he sued doctors Ge and Zhu in the Second Special District Court for manslaughter due to negligence. After the court summoned them, the facts were very clear. The plaintiff twice claimed to be ill and did not appear. Yesterday, the verdict was announced that the two doctors were not negligent.

Male Corpse Found at Jiujiang Road Wharf 191

At around 7:00 PM the night before last, an unidentified male corpse suddenly floated up on the edge of the Jiujiang Road Wharf. He was wearing a gray plaid woolen long gown, white striped trousers, and a black pair of underpants. Next to him were a colored cigarette case and a monk's hairstyle. He was about 30 years old and looked like a merchant. The Chinese police of the Water Police Station discovered it and took the corpse back to the police station. No family members were found to claim it, and the order was sent to the Life Saving Bureau to collect it.

The Four Banks Reserve Vault is jointly established by the Yanye, Jincheng, Zhongnan, and Dalu Banks, specializing in issuing Zhongnan Bank banknotes. According to the vault's issuance regulations, the issuance of banknotes is fully reserved, with cash reserves of at least 60% and guarantee reserves of at most 40%. Record of the Joint Meeting of the Directors and Supervisors of the South Goods Industry Association 193

The South Goods Industry Association held its 32nd joint meeting of directors and supervisors at the City Market yesterday. The attending committee members met the quorum. Jingyan presided over the meeting. After the chairman reported the incoming and outgoing documents, the discussion began. (1) Discussed the letter from the Vocational Trade Union claiming that the Yisheng South Goods Store on Beijing Road, a member, dismissed 11 employees, and the Hengsheng Store on Haiyan Road dismissed three employees, using the Dragon Boat Festival as an excuse for unjustified dismissal and requesting relief. It was resolved that the association would coordinate with the trade union to send staff to investigate the facts and then send a letter to the capital side of the store stating the reasons for the dismissal. (2) According to the report of the Evaluation Committee, Zhenxin Store on Xinzha Road recently moved to Chibang Bridge. Neighboring colleagues Dachang, Dashunchang, and Zhengda interfered with the price of goods, and the evidence was conclusive. Although the association sent staff to advise them, there was no effect. If it is not stopped quickly, it may cause a widening effect, requesting effective suppression. It was resolved that Dachang, Dashunchang, and Zhengda have deliberately violated the association's regulations, and the evidence is conclusive. They will be fined 50 yuan each in accordance with the association's regulations. The association will send a letter to Dashunchang and other stores, requesting them to pay the association within three days. If they still resist the resolution, their City Market licenses will be revoked in accordance with Article 7 of the association's regulations, and their membership qualifications will be canceled in a public announcement. (3) Discussed whether the goods should be increased or decreased. It was resolved to increase eight yards of Tijieqing and sell it for 14.8 cents per catty. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Reading and Answering Questions

How to Learn to Write Letters丨Reply to Mr. Jiang Ziyu丨 197

We used to say that whatever we learn should not be separated from real life, because this can increase the interest in learning and prevent what we learn from being impractical.

This opinion has recently gained the agreement of many readers. Take the readers who discuss the issue of learning writing skills with us. In the past, they discussed learning essays, short articles, novels, poems, dramas, etc. Their method of practicing writing was to arbitrarily create two topics to work on, just like teachers in schools assign compositions to students. The purpose was purely to practice writing techniques. Later, they realized that taking this path was unrealistic, because their own ordinary daily-use writing skills were not even sufficient, and immediately talking about creation was divorced from the practice of life and could not succeed. It would be better to start with letters and diaries, which can be used every day in daily life, and then talk about writing longer pieces later. Because writing letters is both a practice and an application in real life. Learning writing in this direction is of course the most practical. But at the same time, new problems have arisen. They don't know what kind of model to adopt for practice. We have already discussed how to write diaries, so now let's talk about how to write letters!

Based on the books that readers have indicated to us as models for letter writing, they can be roughly divided into two categories: one is classical letters, such as "Xiaocangshanfang Letters," "Qiushuixuan Letters," "Xuehongxuan Letters," etc.; and the other is the most popular vulgar letters, such as "Classified Letters Grand View," "Interpersonal Relations Complete Book," "Rewarding the World Brocade," etc. There are more than these two categories of classical Chinese letters, but most readers only choose these two, which is not accidental. Old-style letters in our country can be divided into three styles. One is the simple letters of the Jin Dynasty, which were mostly used by poets and literati. These letters must have a free and unconventional, elegant and appropriate flavor, otherwise, they would be worthless. This kind of thing is not easy to learn, so it is only popular among scholars. The punctuated and typeset edition of "Su Huang Letters," which has been widely reprinted recently, belongs to this category. Since this kind of letter focuses on elegance, it is naturally not suitable for us ordinary people to emulate. The second type is parallel-prose letters, which were most popular in the officialdom in the past. The style of secretaries was almost always used by subordinates when writing to superiors, because as long as the writing was rich in rhetoric, properly arranged, neatly paired, and sonorous in tone, it was considered superior, and the emptiness of content could be ignored. Superiors had nothing to commend, but in fact, it was necessary to do so. Helpless, they could only use this rotten tune. Now that it is not very popular in officialdom, and we don't need to write "donation appeals" or "essay contests" for others, there are very few people who learn it now. The last type is classical prose letters, which are written in prose. This kind of letter is still used by scholars who admire classical Chinese for communication, but ordinary people rarely use it. It takes a lot of effort to learn these three types of letter writing, and now they are too far removed from our actual lives. Classical letters are based on the social existence of the scholar-officials of feudal society. Their leisurely lives allowed them to show off their rhetoric, which was an elegant thing in their time. If we were to imitate them now, it would be a waste of time and ambition.

Even in letters written in classical prose, there are some works with substantial content, but we still do not recommend that readers take them as models for practicing letter writing, and we do not want readers to adopt this style. The reason is the same as why we must use vernacular Chinese instead of classical Chinese now. The advantage of letter writing over other articles is that it can more truthfully express the author's personal temperament, thoughts, and humor. There is always a bit of affectation in writing other articles, but letter writing is the most naked and straightforward. Therefore, letter writing should use living language. If you use classical Chinese, even if you have the ability to write classical Chinese, it will never be as natural and real as using the language of living people today.

But now the most popular type of letter is the classified letter style, and the book list opened by readers in their letters is mostly this type of book. But it is the most vulgar and rotten thing. The reason why it can have a wide impact on the public is because classical letters are difficult to learn and cannot be emulated by the general public, while it turns some classics into a set of patterns and formats, making it easy for people to copy according to the formula. This type of letter not only mechanically divides the letter into several parts, but also opens up a formula for each part, and arranges it properly according to the social relations of people from "all walks of life." This kind of thing is also inferior in old-style letters. Only people who don't know any better would copy it, and there are many jokes that come out of it! Therefore, although these things are still popular at the moment, they are really not suitable as models for learning letter writing. (To be continued)

Two Work Plans

Proposed by the Provincial Yu Tang Civil Education Hall: (1) Concrete plan for promoting livelihood education. (A) A livelihood education design committee should be organized. (B) The order of implementation of various livelihood education projects should be determined separately based on the social environment and production status. (C) Other education projects should be implemented with livelihood education as the starting point. (D) Regarding the investigation of livelihood aspects, (E) appropriate and effective investigation methods should be adopted. (E) Regarding vocational guidance, (F) vocational guidance centers should be established, (G) vocational training and supplementary classes should be held. (F) Regarding agricultural guidance, (H) the failure of exemplary special agreements and experimental farmland should be remedied. (I) Effective and lasting agricultural improvement associations, agricultural lecture meetings, and agricultural communication agencies should be organized. (J) Agricultural tool and crop exhibitions and cattle competitions should be held. (G) Regarding the promotion of sideline occupations, (A) suitable sideline occupations should be selected and promoted or guided within the implementation area of each hall. (B) The public should be guided to manage sideline occupations in an effective and appropriate manner. (H) Regarding the promotion of cooperation and savings, (A) the public should be guided to organize cooperatives in an effective and appropriate manner. (B) Cooperatives that have been办failed should be rescued and reorganized. (C) The public should be guided to save and economize. (D) The public should be made members of cooperatives. (2) Taking the promotion of cooperative enterprises as the central work plan for livelihood education. (A) Taking the basic implementation area as the area and advocating industrial cooperation with the cooperative enterprise as the population. (B) The cooperative enterprise in the promotion area should have a de facto connection with the cooperative center organization in the basic implementation area.

(1) A case where ordinary farmers are unwilling to answer truthfully to livelihood surveys should be remedied. (2) The implementation of livelihood education is a specialized undertaking. Language Education Category

Modern Thought Society Solicits Essays Youth in China Responds Enthusiastically 214

The Topic is Whether China Can Implement Dictatorial Politics

The Modern Thought Society, in order to test the political views of young people in China, held an essay solicitation event a month ago. The topic was whether China can implement dictatorial politics. Since the news was published, young people in China have responded enthusiastically. The society has recently received more than 50 essays from young people in Beijing, Tianjin, Hankou, Nanchang, Nanjing, Jinan, Guangzhou, Shanghai and other places. Most of them are college students, followed by middle school students and young people in the professional world. For the sake of prudence, the society hired Wang Yunwu, Pan Gongzhan, Yang Gongda, Wu Yaxian, Chen Gaorong, Wu Kaixian, Lin Zhongke, Tong Hangbai, Ding Mocun, Tao Baichuan, Jiang Huaixu, Ma Chonggan, Hu Shuyi, Huang Tianpeng, Jiang Xiangqing, Wang Xinming, Xu Zexiang, Zhu Yixin, Xue Guangqian, Xu Xingchu, and Huang Xianggu, etc., divided them into two groups, A and B, and organized an evaluation committee to decide on the ranking. Special Article

The Classical Chinese Movement in Primary and Secondary Schools (II) 222

— Wang Maozu

"To make the Chinese nation a people of great benevolence, wisdom, and courage, we must first establish the foundation of loyalty, filial piety, integrity, and righteousness, and then seek its deficiencies in knowledge and skills. We should value martial arts to prepare for military qualifications and emphasize practicality to warn against the frivolous and superficial customs of the end of the dynasty. We must possess loyalty, taking patriotism as the prerequisite, and cultivate determination, taking idleness as the greatest taboo. Those who say this should be ashamed of being inferior to others." These words came from Yuan Shikai. All those who say this after Yuan Shikai are Yuan Shikai. Moreover, our country's historical relics are all legacies of the feudal era, and should be regarded with as little regard as "boundless trees shedding their leaves, rustling down." Then it is no wonder that students' minds today are chaotic and unable to distinguish between black and white. How can we expect scientific progress? The impact of enlightening students with such thoughts is significant, and it is not merely a debate between vernacular and classical Chinese.

(III) Mr. Wu argues that prohibiting the study of classical Chinese is not the personal opinion of a few, and lists the previous Ministry of Education, the former University Council, and the current Ministry of Education, citing the opinions of many ministers, vice ministers, and ministry members, who have advocated prohibiting primary schools from studying classical Chinese. These grand decrees are not something that a few people can take over." I do not know if this is precisely evidence of the opinion of the few. As for the decrees of the ministry, we who serve in the education sector should obey them. If we still promote "administrative academicization," then I dare not remain silent. Moreover, not all ministers agree with Mr. Wu. Only the former Vice Minister Liu Jun Dabai advocated the vernacular most strongly, creating strange terms such as "human language (vernacular) ghost language (classical Chinese)" to suppress public opinion. At that time, Mr. Wu was able to express his aspirations greatly, but Mr. Liu is now deceased, and classical Chinese has not died with him. The current Minister Wang Jun is knowledgeable and erudite, but his skills are specialized, and his efforts are focused on long-term goals. He may not have a strong interest in what we are debating. What I hope for from Mr. Wang is that he can correct the mistakes of his predecessors. If it is said that the grand decrees cannot be easily changed, then there have been countless instances of the Ministry's decrees being amended or revoked. If he accepts falsehoods and errors and sits idly by while they flow downstream, I fear for this. The mistakes of a gentleman are like the eclipse of the sun and moon, and people look up to him when he corrects them. This is true of individuals, and it should be true of the government. If the current officials of the Ministry of Education do not believe the opinions of men of letters and scholars, please investigate the needs of the professions, and you will surely know that what I say is not without reason.

With the the order of, also from the school principals primary school principals who know who has violated the order, and more troublesome to the Ministry's, reading the classics is by no means a bad thing, it seems today to make the provincial authorities how Chen advocated the scriptures can be

Mr. Wu, under that, China talent, to add column, educators are not just, educators, fortunately note.

(IV) It is of course good that primary schools use vernacular teaching materials, but are the stories of birds and animals, and the absurd and fantastical tales, consistent with the intention of most departments to promote science? This can still be explained by children's interests. It is not appropriate to use them in the first and second grades of primary school, in order to arouse children's interest. The use of such materials must be deeply enlightening. As for indicative matters and names, there is no need for this. If cats, dogs, chickens, and sheep eat, dress, and speak, it is permissible to use chapters to amuse children. This is what is called a sugar-coated interest. Dewey also criticized its inappropriateness. Allegorical teaching materials can certainly be without stories, but the attitude must be if cats are also called gentlemen, children's thoughts will be deceived by this kind of humor. No true friends. Recently, a friend's child, in the first grade of a certain primary school, one day, the grade taught the story of monsters eating people, ordering two children to dress up as monsters in another room. The teacher led the entire class to drive away the monsters, and some children were frightened and cried. The purpose of this lesson was to cultivate a fearless spirit, but the children did not know what monsters were, so they were deliberately given terrible stimulation to arouse their instinct of fear, and the result was the opposite of the purpose. Is this how education should be?

Recently, I happened to find the following excerpt from the 14th lesson of the fourth volume of the Elementary School Chinese Textbook published by a certain bureau:

Three Little Squirrels

(I) Looking at Clothes 223

There are three little squirrels, one called Red Tail, one called Blue Eyes, and one called Yellow Fur. They know that Children's Day is coming soon, and they are discussing what clothes to wear to school for the meeting.

Red Tail took out a red coat, sighed, and said, "I always wear red coats. It's really annoying. I want to choose another color." Blue Eyes took out a blue jacket, shook his head, and said, "I've worn this blue jacket too. It's best to change to another color." Yellow Fur took out a yellow cheongsam and said, "I also hate this yellow cheongsam. It would be best if I could change to another color."

Red Tail said, "Let's ask Miss Butterfly. The color of her clothes is the best. Maybe she will tell us how to change colors." Blue Eyes and Yellow Fur both said, "Great, great!" They decided and went to Miss Butterfly's house to find her.

(II) Changing Colors

The three squirrels found Miss Butterfly and discussed with her how to change the colors.

The butterfly thought for a day and then flapped its wings and said, "I have an idea! There are several ponds behind the forest. You take your clothes and wash them, and maybe they will change color."

They listened and went to find the ponds. They found three ponds, one with yellow water, one with red water, and one with blue water. Red Tail's red coat, each squirrel took their own clothes to wash. Red Tail's red coat was washed in the yellow water pond, Blue Eyes' blue jacket was washed in the red water pond, and Yellow Fur's yellow cheongsam was washed in the blue water pond. In less than five minutes, they said, they took the clothes up and wrung them dry. Red Tail looked and jumped up and said, "Oh, it really changed! My red coat has become the color of orange peel." Blue Eyes was also very surprised, tilted his tail, and said, "Look, my blue jacket has also changed. It's purple, how beautiful!" Yellow Fur looked at her cheongsam and said, "Look, hasn't it changed too? This is green."

Everyone was very happy to see it.

(III) Changing Names

On Children's Day, the three little squirrels wore beautiful clothes and came to school for the meeting. Red Tail wore an orange coat, Blue Eyes wore a purple jacket, and Yellow Fur wore a green cheongsam.

The children saw them and seemed not to recognize them. Everyone said, "The clothes worn by these three girls are really beautiful!"

At the potluck, the three little squirrels told the children about how they changed the color of their clothes.

The main point here, in addition to seeking special colors and explaining the principles of color matching and color matching, is to know what kind of feelings it can evoke. If Children's Day is explained from the children's own perspective, it will be more authentic. Why create monsters like Red Tail and Green Eyes? Changing clothes to attend meetings and potlucks, it's as if today's textbooks require all kinds of knowledge to come from the mouths of various animals. This is also strange. The United States also has a faction that vigorously exaggerates the value of myths and stories, which is called the Romantic School. The romantic textbooks in our country are not seen as romantic. The accumulation of errors can become right. This is why Confucius hated purple for taking away from vermilion.

(V) Dewey advocated "education is life" and deeply criticized the preparation of life. This meaning is often misunderstood, leading to an overemphasis on children's lives and indifference to their future needs. In fact, Dewey's education is life. The meaning does not contain the intention of preparation. What he opposed was teaching children completely from the perspective of adults. It is a pity that Mr. Dewey's criticism of "preparing for life" was excessive, resulting in great abuses, which was not expected. The period of compulsory education in various countries is relatively long, and it is still possible to calmly focus on children's lives. If our country's compulsory education is only four years, it is still unattainable. In these four years, it seems appropriate to pay more attention to "preparation." All social needs should be emphasized, and the rural environment should be considered. The current textbooks focus on the lives of urban children, which is not reasonable, and the words that are rarely used in society are found in the first volume, such as the 10th and 11th lessons of a certain bureau's textbook.

Old Hen "Cluck, cluck, cluck" Little Chicken "Cheep, cheep, cheep" 224

How many times will these two words " and " " be used in a lifetime, and must we first teach them to recognize them? In my opinion, this type of textbook, even the vernacular in the lower grades, must be rewritten before it can be used.

In society, there is opposition to storybooks. I initially thought that the words of men of letters and scholars were not credible, so I ignored them. Returning to my hometown last year for inspection, I realized that this type of textbook is even more opposed in rural areas, and everyone says that studying in private schools is useful. A few days ago, the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs convened a vocational guidance meeting, with representatives from agriculture, industry, and commerce attending. They all advocated that classical Chinese must be taught in senior primary schools, and some even supported private schools. From an educational perspective, we cannot be too accommodating to the environment. However, in the thirty years since the establishment of modern schools, private schools have not only not been eliminated but have also been on the rise. This is also enough to cause us to reflect deeply. This is why I wrote this article. (To be continued)

Literary Corner

Records of Imperial Incense's Vague Fragrance 225

— Original by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

I said: "Really, the weather is too cold! It's time to wear fur coats! Ancestor." (Translator's note: It is said that Princess Rong Ling said: The people in the palace originally called Empress Dowager Cixi the Old Buddha, but later, because Emperor Kangxi also had the title of "Old Buddha" on that day, it was changed to Ancestor. This reference is very appropriate.) "I think it's perfectly fine to wear fur coats tomorrow. Why doesn't the Empress Dowager issue an imperial edict now?"

What luck! Not only did these few words of mine not offend her, but they immediately gained her sympathy. Thus, the imperial edict "From tomorrow onwards, everyone must wear fur coats" was issued without delay.

The next day, throughout the entire territory of the Manchu Qing Empire, as long as there were officials and noblewomen who were qualified to wear fur coats, they all put them on. And my new dress instantly became the most fashionable and eye-catching winter outfit! I thought: When the weather was so cold, if I hadn't taken this courageous action, others wouldn't have been able to wear fur coats even if they wanted to. How grateful would they be to me!

But on the other hand, I thought, all for the sake of my wanting to wear that new dress with fur trim, I urged the Empress Dowager to issue the edict to wear fur coats. After this edict was issued, I don't know how many people were kept busy all night!

When I was in the palace, every day there were many new clothes. Some eunuchs put them on wooden trays and carried them in for the Empress Dowager to see. There were always many tailors supported in the palace, and these tailors absolutely dared not be lazy. Therefore, the Empress Dowager's new clothes were being made continuously. However, this time when she went to Fengtian, she did not bring those tailors along.

In the palace, there was also a group of elderly women with a long history and mysterious movements. They ate their fill all day long and did no work. They just lowered their heads every day and held pens to draw patterns for the Empress Dowager's new shoes. This time, the Empress Dowager did not load them onto the boat to Fengtian either. (62)

Chaozhou Opera 226

— Nai Ling

People in Shanghai are probably very unfamiliar with Chaozhou opera, right? Although there are some Chaozhou songs on records, the "ee-ee-yah-yah" tunes are not only unfamiliar to Shanghai people, but I don't think anyone would enjoy listening to them, let alone understand them!

Recently, a group of Chaozhou opera performers came to Shanghai and have been performing in a certain theater in the French Concession for more than ten days.

I didn't have time to listen to them, even though I can understand them. So I estimate that most of the people who specially went to a certain theater to listen to Chaozhou opera are those Chaozhou people living in Shanghai, especially a group of idle old ladies and young women.

I remember when I was a child, I was very enthusiastic about Chaozhou opera. Before the play even started, I would often run backstage and peek through the railing at the "opera teacher" teaching the actors.

What makes Chaozhou opera most special from other places is that the actors in Chaozhou opera are all children aged seven or eight to fifteen or sixteen, the so-called "child actors." These children are bought by the opera troupe owners for a few hundred yuan, or someone hands the child over to the opera troupe, specifying the years. When the term is up, the child can gain freedom.

The "opera teacher" is also hired by the owner, and his power is the greatest. When teaching children to act, if they do not meet his expectations, he will not be polite with bamboo boards and whips. Sometimes, a child who has been acting for several years becomes disabled when he regains his freedom. This is not uncommon. Even if they are not disabled, but have been suppressed for several years, once they come to society, they have no ability to work and end up wandering as vagrants. Otherwise, they can only live as "street singers" like beggars.

However, it is said that this kind of tragic phenomenon is now relatively rare!

A Scene of Seeking a Child 227

— Wang Shouqiu

The bricklayer Wang from the same street is almost forty years old this year, but he still doesn't have a single child. Although the bricklayer Wang's wife has prayed to gods and temples, burned incense and made vows, and stolen the little clay dolls in front of the Child-Giving Goddess, but year after year has passed, the belly of the bricklayer Wang's wife is still flat and has not bulged up. This clearly shows that the bricklayer Wang's efforts to seek a child have failed just like this year's Women's National Goods Year!

The more the bricklayer Wang's wife's belly doesn't bulge, the more the bricklayer Wang hopes it will bulge, and the more urgent the thought of wanting it to bulge becomes. Probably last month, the bricklayer Wang implemented another kind of child-seeking work, dragging his wife across seven ditches, which is indeed an interesting piece of news.

The fact is like this: I don't know which day last month, the bricklayer Wang invited several colleagues and waited in an open space. And the bricklayer Wang himself? He tricked his wife into coming. Taking advantage of her unpreparedness, he suddenly pushed her down. Then his colleagues, one person grabbing one of her feet, desperately dragged her forward. While dragging, they asked her "Are you going to have a child?" "Are you going to have a child?" His wife was too embarrassed to say that she would, so she ignored them. The bricklayer Wang was really anxious at this time, fearing that he would fall short of success, so he forced her to say it. Although she was shy, she finally succumbed because of her husband's coercion and the pain in her back. And she said: "I'm going to have a child!" "I'm going to have a child!" Only then did she lower her head and run home in the cheers of the crowd. But four or five pieces of skin had been scraped off her back! And she didn't come out for half a month because of this incident.

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast 229

Chapter 30: Seeing the Wretched Wild Geese Off, He Buried Himself in Defending the Territory; A Bullet Pierced a Strong Arm, Dyeing the Blood Red

Zi Qiang called the squad leader over in the starlight and cold wind, said a few words himself, and immediately came to the battalion headquarters. In Fang's office, two foreign candles were already lit on the clay brick table. He unfolded a military map in the candlelight. He pressed it with both hands, bent down, and was standing there looking at it. Zhao Ziqiang saluted and stood still in the candlelight. Bao Fang said: Wait a moment, I have orders. The enemy seems to be planning to invade our North Gate by detouring. The first company of this battalion will set off immediately, exit the North Gate, and defend the first line of trenches. Taking advantage of the darkness and unpreparedness, wait for the enemy to approach and use extremely powerful artillery fire to resolutely resist. I will be at the battalion headquarters. After he finished, the company commanders received their orders, saluted, and withdrew. Yin Deren was in the first company. When he returned to his company headquarters, he blew his whistle and gathered all the soldiers in the company to stand in formation. Under the starlight, he used a flashlight to shine on the roster and called their names. Then he gave a lecture to all the soldiers in the company: Brothers, now is our opportunity to work hard to kill the bandits. We have received reports that there are very few enemies, not even a company's worth, coming to attack our defensive positions. This situation is clearly a contempt for our uselessness. Tasting Dung 230

— Jin Shude

I remember when I was in the capital, my neighbor Ding Jirong's wife could be considered a first-class shrew in the city. She usually abused her parents-in-law the most. When her husband returned, she would complain and say that it was her parents-in-law who were wrong. Her husband was a businessman, quite literate, and also knew something about filial piety. However, after being influenced by this shrew for a long time, sometimes his filial piety would change and he would follow the wind, just to please his wife. One day, her husband returned and heard her say that her parents-in-law were wrong again. Her husband had no choice but to give her an answer that he didn't quite believe, thinking that this would be the end of it. Who knew that she thought that her husband was not helping her, so she took advantage of people's unpreparedness, tidied herself up, and lay stiffly on the bed, half-opening and half-closing her eyes, without making a sound. Her husband inadvertently entered the room and, seeing this situation, was so frightened that his soul left his body. He hurriedly called for his parents and neighbors, relatives, and so on, shouting loudly and softly, but she still didn't make a sound. In the end, everyone carefully inspected her and found that she was missing an earring from her left ear. Everyone thought that she had swallowed gold to kill herself. The neighbors knew about her usual behavior, so they all said in unison that dung juice should be poured into her stomach from her mouth. The gold would be vomited out. At this time, she became anxious and tossed and turned on the bed, refusing to taste the smelly dung. Everyone didn't say a word, and tied her up with seven hands and eight feet, pried open her teeth, and poured about a cigarette can of dung juice into her mouth. In the end, nothing was vomited out. I interrupted and pretended to say that I had seen this trick in Shanghai and simply threatened her, saying: "Unless you find foreigners to cut open your stomach, there's no way." She was extremely frightened and搶抢抢 said, "Don't, I was just trying to scare my husband. I had hidden the earring under the floor in advance." Only then did the family slowly put down the stone in their hearts.

Small Talk

On Dogs (Continued) 231

— Bing Yu

Feeding utensils must be kept clean. Each feeding should provide an even amount of food; do not overfeed. For puppies around three months old, feed five to seven times a day. At five months, feed four to five times. At seven months, feed three to four times. For a one-year-old dog, feed twice a day, morning and evening. Puppies are naturally innocent and love to chew on stones and wood chips. Normally, you can give them some charcoal and beef bones to gnaw on, to prevent them from chewing on stones and damaging their digestive system. Each time you feed them, you can teach them various tricks, such as standing, sitting, lying down, and somersaulting. To prevent the accumulation of dirt in their fur, you should regularly brush them clean. In summer, bathe them every other day. (4) Considerations for Nursing: If puppies are born to your own female dog, they usually open their eyes around ten days old, and can see things around twenty days old, and can also stand. Between twenty and thirty days after birth, their milk teeth gradually grow, and their claws become sharp. The mother dog's nipples are often bitten by their teeth or scratched by their claws, and she gradually becomes averse to them nursing. After fifty days, the amount of breast milk decreases, and gradually feed them easily digestible foods. For the first week after birth, puppies should not be exposed to excessive external stimuli or extreme cold or heat. The temperature of the food and the surroundings of the doghouse should not be too hot or too cold. After twenty days, they can walk. At this time, they will certainly like to lie in the sun to get plenty of sunshine, in order to promote development. If there are any that cannot develop due to their tail, then depending on the breed of dog, the tail can be cut off. (5) Exercise: The owner should often take the dog outside for walks every day and never keep it indoors all day long, which is too restrictive and causes it to lose its natural instincts. Schedule a certain trick to teach them every day, cycling through them. This can help them exercise and also practice their skills. As rain is something dogs hate the most, their food intake should be reduced to avoid indigestion. (6) Nursing When Sick: Because we are in daily contact with dogs, we can easily understand their constitution and nature, the condition of their feces, and the state of their spirit. If the body is thin, when sleeping, they try to get up and walk, but after walking a few steps, they want to lie down again. Their food intake decreases, their noses are very dry, or they have nasal discharge, or they cough, have difficulty breathing, have a lot of eye discharge, the whites of their eyes look bloodshot, or they are pale due to anemia, their abdomen is swollen, their feces are thin, or they often vomit, or they are losing hair, these are signs of illness. However, the origins of dog diseases are often when the weather is warm and hot, when fleas, lice, mosquitoes, and other pests are most abundant, or during the humid plum rain season. During this period, the dog's life functions gradually change, skin diseases may occur, and parasites may enter the stomach and intestines through food, and various diseases follow. The most serious diseases are distemper, heart disease (Detenber), pneumonia, and common cold cough. These diseases are often fatal. Chinese people have traditionally not valued dogs. Once they get sick, they only use bird medicine. Based on my experience raising dogs, if they have a cold or cough, you can give them medicines to relieve the exterior and stop coughing, but the medicinal liquid is very difficult to administer. It is best to buy powder and administer it from the corner of the mouth. This is what my veterinarian friend taught me. He said that the life functions of dogs are originally the same as those of humans, and ordinary diseases can be completely treated according to the methods of treating people. Later, I repeatedly verified this through trials. When sick, the food fed should be nutritious, liquid, and easily digestible. If a dog has rickets, it should be fed more foods rich in Vitamin D and Calcium (Calcium, a silvery-white metallic element, a nourishing supplement). However, dogs hate things with a bad smell. You can mix the medicine with cream and their favorite food, so that they can take it.

Unfavorable Financial News; Gold Price Slips Slightly by 7 Candareens; Only 1.8 Taels Traded in One Day 232

Yesterday, although there were no fluctuations in the overseas silver market, reports indicated that India was willing to cooperate with the U.S. government to promote silver coinage in the hope of raising the price of silver. Foreign dispatches also stated that the silver bill had been signed by the U.S. President. The market was sluggish today. In the morning, with no ups or downs in the British and American overseas silver markets, the prices of forward silver on the Precious Metals Exchange showed mixed signals of rise and fall, exchange rates contracted, London gold was flat, U.S. cotton fell slightly, and U.S. wheat rose by 0.75. Stocks showed mixed rises and falls. Both Sin Fung Hong and Reuters reported that President Roosevelt would sign or had already signed the silver bill. Preliminary trading retreated to 13.04 taels. After the opening, the situation was flat and weak. Then, because the domestic market went from flat to slightly tight, Guang Bang (Cantonese merchants) in the market continued to purchase strips, gradually turning stable. Decaying Atmosphere Spreads Throughout Shanghai; No New Developments in the Silver and Banking Industries 234

In recent years, the entire Shanghai market has felt the economic decline, with various industries in dire straits, leading to a decaying atmosphere spreading throughout the city. This has resulted in the financial sector having no loans to extend, and even when loans are extended, they cannot be fully expanded and developed. Furthermore, there is a pervasive sense of risk and deception, and with the value of goods depressed, extending loans is naturally difficult. Therefore, all transactions with various industries are consistently approached with caution, with no opportunities for expansion. If this continues, and with the approaching summer slack season, a more frigid state is feared. Yesterday's interbank lending rate was slightly better than the previous day, at 7 points, consistent between morning and afternoon. However, transactions in drafts were inferior to the previous few days. Morning market transfers were only over 3.5 million, with new transactions over 300,000. Afternoon market transactions were over 400,000. Transactions at the Small General Association were over 300,000. The market rate for "yang hua tou" (foreign coin head) plus water (premium) was still no more than 0.02 or 0.03 points, and the transaction situation remained sluggish. Transactions in foreign pawn loans totaled 780,000, but the actual amount made was even less. Furthermore, banknotes brought back from Jiangbei and Hankou totaled 340,000 in exchange for silver certificates, mostly Chinese banknotes. There was no information on outward remittances. Bank clearings: Foreign banks cleared 2.78 million in draft funds, 4.34 million in various goods and foreign exchange collateral, and 2.56 million in semi-annual settlements, with 400,000 in warehouse withdrawals. Cotton Yarn: Marked Yarn Continues to Trend Higher 238

The yarn market, after initially showing signs of fatigue, has once again become tense with rising prices. This is due to high prices for Japanese yarn. Speculators in the market generally believe that the Sino-Japanese dispute is likely to be resolved peacefully, and the issues of postal and transportation services are expected to be settled by July 1st. As a result, those betting on rising prices have become very active. Furthermore, merchants from Tianjin have been consistently purchasing Chinese yarn, leading to a shift in sentiment. The market is cautiously optimistic about future changes, adjusting sales based on actual demand.

Golden Rooster Bullish Activity

At the opening of the marked yarn pre-market, American cotton prices fell in terms of pounds. However, the previous day's bullish momentum led to a slight shortage of buyers in the market, with prices for each month (May, June, and July) falling by five, six, and seven tenths of a tael. Around noon, the cotton market rallied, driving yarn prices up by several tenths of a tael. Grains: Signs of Decline in the Flour Market 243

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning, prices for all months showed a consistent decline. Imported wheat was quoted at Chicago at slightly higher prices (one or two corners) and Canada (two or three corners). However, market sentiment was influenced by the heavy rain the previous night, with continued rainfall the following day. With rice seedlings being transplanted everywhere, this welcome rain not only pleased farmers but also eased the minds of those involved in the grain trade. As a result, prices declined after the opening, with near months falling by nearly one tenth of a tael and distant months by two tenths of a tael. By the afternoon closing, prices for the current month had fallen by nearly one tenth of a tael again. Distant months, however, were supported by buying from the banking sector, causing the market to recover slightly. Under the current circumstances, actual sales are still being observed, while speculative activity continues unabated. Only a surge in physical goods will break this trend. Ultimately, the current month fell by 0.05 tael, July and August fell by 0.125 tael, September fell by 0.1 tael, October fell by 0.15 tael, and November fell by 0.1 tael.

Flat and Sluggish Wheat Futures 244

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat futures market in the morning and afternoon, prices for all months generally showed a flat and sluggish trend. Imported wheat prices were slightly higher (one, two, or three corners). However, the rain had eased the minds of traders in both local and foreign markets, weakening market sentiment after the opening. Although new wheat is being harvested, farmers are busy with autumn farming, and supplies have not been flowing smoothly. As a result, both sellers and buyers have been hesitant. However, it is predicted that supplies will improve in about two weeks, and market fluctuations should be observed at that time. Ultimately, July fell by 0.02 tael, August fell by 0.01 tael, and September fell by 0.03 tael. The spot wheat market is stable. While shipments are arriving continuously, this year's wheat is mostly dry, and both buyers and sellers are unwilling to accept discounts. Therefore, prices are being maintained. Lin Huai, Mingguang, and Bengbu wheat are priced at 1.9 taels. Wuhu, Gaoyou, Hezhou, and Liuhe wheat are priced at 2.8 taels. Kunshan wheat is priced at 2.7 taels, up to 2.65 taels. Zhitang wheat is priced at 1.75 taels. Fuxin purchased 1,700 packages, Xinda purchased 1,000 packages, Shenda purchased 1,000 packages, and Huafeng purchased 1,000 packages.

Active Retail Sales of He Xia Rice 245

(Hu Nan) Arrivals are extremely scarce, with only about a dozen firms (a total of 1,400 shi), making the situation quite tight. Retail sales are slow in the market, and sellers are demanding high prices, leading to continued sluggish market conditions. However, wholesale buyers are discouraged by reports of falling prices in Tianjin, so they are only purchasing about 1,000 packages, keeping the market flat. The prices of glutinous rice have risen by over a foot in various stores throughout the city, and indica rice has also seen increases of several tenths of a tael. Bagged rice remains unaffected. Du Yang’s superior quality rice continues to be sought after due to its superior quality, while older rice has been slightly cheaper, but has also seen prices increase by a few tenths of a tael.

(Hu Bei) Yesterday, the supply of He Xia rice was only six or seven firms. While retail sales were not good, wholesalers remained firm. As a result, the price of white glutinous rice increased by an angle, early season indica increased as well, Du yang's superior quality rice increased as well, other rice types were stable.

Silk & Tea: Strong Demand for Dried Cocoons, Silk Sales Remain Clear 246

Green cocoon production is not weak. This year's Jiaxing spring silkworm eggs are not weak, resulting in a relatively abundant cocoon harvest. Traditional varieties account for 60%, while improved varieties account for 40%. The total production of fresh cocoons in the county is over 60,000 dan, accounting for one-third of the province's total production.

There are over hundreds of cocoon firms. Firms have collected of the improve variety cocoons, hundred fifty-seven dan and fifty-five jin. The local cocoon varieties are forty thousand hundreds forty-eight dan and seven hundred six jin. There are more than ten thousand dan that villagers use to spin soil silk. Within the cocoon there are over nine hundreds dan of mixed color cocoons.

Suzhou Cocoons are Continuously Transported Suzhou Spring Cocoons have come to an end. The silk cocoon merchants in the port bake fresh cocoons into dried cocoons for shipping to Shanghai. In recent days, the new cocoons from Yixing, Liyang, Changshu, Wuxi, and Chengjiang counties have been transported with over forty thousands packages where Suzhou transport covers three ten thousands packages. Shanghai Ningbo trains only loaded over a ten thousands packages.

Silk Sales Remain Difficult to Turn Around The European and American markets are importing silk. The current prices are stagnant. There are thick inventories but imports remain. The current price of silk is dropping. The Shanghai port sent telegrams that the price is too high and it does not convert. Although the Europeans are stocking up, the price is very low, Chinese businessmen can not sell. Silk sales remain lacking a turning point. Yesterday Dachan and other companies sent hundreds of yellow and white silk to Shanghai. The price remained the same.

Pingshui Big Firms Have Already Opened 247

Zhejiang’s Shaoxing Pingshui green tea has seen improvement of its sales recently. Colorless people from the local area and continue to continue the board game. The city has a total of three Gangs, including Jiatian Zhenheng, where the highest price is fifty yuan, zero and a corner, and the lowest price is forty-eight yuan and seven corners. The average price is six to seven yuan lower than last year. Other Zhenmei pearl teas and various small colors have also improved. In addition, Luzhuang Zhenmei needle teas are trading lively. Jiangxi Province's Yushan Zhenmei has been opened for bidding by Zhenhe Tea Company at a price of eighty yuan, and the selling price is also quite firm. For black teas such as Qining, both the British and Russian companies have strong purchasing power, and the market trend is stable. However, a large amount of Hubei black tea has recently been shipped from Hankou to Shanghai, making it difficult to stabilize the situation.
